## Contexts in which the phrase **papua new guinea** was used in the Senate during the 1970s

* A statement by the Minister for External Territories dated 27th April 1971 relating to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Constitutional Development [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1971/19710427_senate_27_s47/#subdebate-55-0)

* When a Bill of this character comes before this chamber we should register our continuing and persistent interest in and identification with <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> and the contribution that Australia is making to the development of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1971/19710511_senate_27_s48/#subdebate-64-0)

* I know that we are charged sometimes regarding our contributions to the development of underdeveloped countries, but our contribution is high, particularly when we take into account our contribution to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1971/19710511_senate_27_s48/#subdebate-64-0)

* The Government has accepted the Committee's report, as endorsed by the House of Assembly, as reflecting the views of the people of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1971/19710518_senate_27_s48/#subdebate-40-0)

* What companies hold petroleum prospecting licences (a) onshore; and (b) offshore in the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> region? [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1971/19710818_senate_27_s49/#subdebate-49-0)

* How many petroleum prospective basins have been identified in the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> region: and of these, in respect of how many have (a) prospecting licences already been granted: and (b) applications been called for? [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1971/19710818_senate_27_s49/#subdebate-49-0)

* What are the locations and acreages of national parks and wildlife sanctuaries in
              <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>? [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1971/19710908_senate_27_s49/#subdebate-49-0)

* I also inform the Senate that the Minister for External Territories,  Mr Barnes,  will be in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> this week. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1971/19711123_senate_27_s50/#debate-0)

* Will the Territory of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> security and intelligence service maintain surveillance of elected members of the Territory House of Assembly and of members of the Mataungan Association. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1971/19711210_senate_27_s50/#subdebate-47-0)

* The first is a statement by the Minister for External Territories  (Mr Peacock)  on the sale of the Commonwealth equity in Commonwealth-New Guinea Timbers Ltd, and the second is a statement by the Minister for External Territories on recent events in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720509_senate_27_s52/#subdebate-36-3)

* I wish to draw the attention of honourable senators to the fact that  Mr Perry  Kwan, the  Speaker  of the House of Assembly of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>, is present in the President's gallery at my invitation. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720523_senate_27_s52/#debate-1)

* For the information of honourable senators, I present the report to the General Assembly of the United Nations on the administration of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> for the year ended 30th June 1971. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720530_senate_27_s52/#debate-31)

* This one is the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Bill 1972 and the second one is the New Guinea Timber Agreement Act (Repeal) Bill 1972. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720824_senate_27_s53/#subdebate-48-0)

* There is no opposition to this <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Bill which deals with the removal of the limitation on the number of offices of ministers of the House of Assembly of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> which can be created by the Minister for External Territories  (Mr Peacock). [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720824_senate_27_s53/#subdebate-48-0)

* However in these times of growing development in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> obviously the current base of 17 members is much too low. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720824_senate_27_s53/#subdebate-48-0)

* The Australian Government has for many years adopted the attitude that no obstacle should be placed in the way of a smooth and orderly transition to self government in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720824_senate_27_s53/#subdebate-48-0)

* A lot of restrictions have been placed on the House of Assembly in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> by the current Government. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720824_senate_27_s53/#subdebate-48-0)

* Now as <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> stands on the threshold of independence this Bill is right and proper. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720824_senate_27_s53/#subdebate-48-0)

* I believe that the long term result of the removal of this limitation and the fulfilling of the desire of the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> House of Assembly to expand its ministry must react in the favour of Australia. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720824_senate_27_s53/#subdebate-48-1)

* Democracy at long last will have a free go in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720824_senate_27_s53/#subdebate-48-1)

* I remind  Senator wheat-growing  Young, who is trying to interject, that another Bill dealing with <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> will come before the Senate immediately after this Bill is passed. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720824_senate_27_s53/#subdebate-48-1)

* It has a great deal to do with your sell-out of products to your Australian friends in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720824_senate_27_s53/#subdebate-48-1)

* I ask the Minister representing the Minister for External Territories: Has any approach been made by Japan to set up a consulate in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>? [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720829_senate_27_s53/#subdebate-3-0)

* I am without information as to the availability of eggs and egg products in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> at the present time, but I will most willingly refer the honourable senator's suggestion to the attention of the Minister for External Territories so that consideration can be given to the inclusion of these foods in any further shipment. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19721012_senate_27_s54/#subdebate-27-0)

* My question, which is directed to the Minister representing the Minister for External Territories, arises from the answer he has just given to the Senate concerning emergency food supplies for <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19721012_senate_27_s54/#subdebate-27-0)

* In view of the over production of eggs in Australia, why were eggs and egg products not included in the supplies which were sent to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>? [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19721012_senate_27_s54/#subdebate-27-0)

* Will he give an undertaking to give some consideration to the forwarding of eggs and egg products to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>? [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19721012_senate_27_s54/#subdebate-27-0)

* I ask the Leader of the Government in the Senate: In view of the serious drought prevailing in the highland area of New Guinea and coinciding with the delicate negotiations for independence, will the Minister indicate what measures are being taken by the Australian Government to assist the Government of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> in alleviating this most unfortunate situation? [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19721012_senate_27_s54/#subdebate-24-0)

* Australia has protested to the Government of the Republic of China on a number of occasions, the latest being a protest over the recent incursions of Taiwanese fishing vessels into the fishing zones of Australia and <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19721025_senate_27_s54/#subdebate-67-0)

* you recognise that we are Australians and do not wish to become citizens of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>; [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730228_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-0-1)

* Was the statement made by the Minister on the establishment of a para-military force of 3,500 persons to maintain the security of the Territory of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> in the immediate future issued as a result of a Cabinet decision; if not, why was the statement made and has it now been countermanded. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730328_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-56-0)

* I have not issued a statement on the establishment of a para-military force of 3,500 persons to maintain the security of the Territory of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> in the immediate future. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730328_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-56-0)

* Has the Commonwealth Government approved a relaxation of quarantine regulations to permit the admission of cats and dogs from <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>, Norfolk Island, Hawaii and Fiji. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730329_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-58-0)

* Is rabies endemic in Indonesia; if so, is there a strong likelihood of the spread of this disease from animals in West Irian to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> and what added precautions have been taken by the Departments concerned to ensure positive safeguards against the introduction of this disease into Australia. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730329_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-58-0)

* The quarantine regulations have been amended to permit the admission of cats and dogs from <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>, Norfolk Island, Hawaii and Fiji under certain conditions. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730329_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-58-0)

* Rabies is endemic in parts of Indonesia but is not reported to be present in the provinces east of Java, including West Irian, so it is not considered that there is a strong likelihood of the introduction of rabies into <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> from West Irian. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730329_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-58-0)

* The conditions for importation of dogs and cats from <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> (and Norfolk Island, Hawaii and Fiji) include a quarantine period in Australia of nine months. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730329_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-58-0)

* We recognise that in a developing country such as <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> the transport of goods is an essential priority and that it is of prime importance to acquire sufficient finance to construct roads. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730412_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-43-0)

* However, I am quite confident that, with the passage of time, not withstanding the events which we know will be forthcoming shortly, the Australian Government will not abrogate its responsibility towards <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730522_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-48-0)

* In his closing remarks  Senator Byrne  made the comment that Australia shared a sense of responsibility with <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730522_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-48-0)

* As  Senator Young,  has said, the Minister has given us no information at all about the future of consultation on this matter, not only between Australia and <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> but also between the Commonwealth and the Australian State governments which have a vital interest in this matter. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730523_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-39-0)

* My question is in regard to the judges of the Supreme Court of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730606_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-42-0)

* 1 presume that these Bills have no particular application to the position of the judges of the Supreme Court of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>, but they no doubt must have some of the same concern that public servants have in regard to independence and to what their position will be after independence. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730606_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-42-0)

* I ask the Attorney-General  (Senator Murphy)  when replying to the debate to define certain points for me in relation to the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> (Staffing Assistance) Bill. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730606_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-42-0)

* The Commonwealth Banks Act is the third of the Australian Acts relating to banking which extend to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731017_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-48-0)

* This Act is being amended to provide that at a date to be determined, <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> would be excluded from the operation of the Act. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731017_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-48-0)

* This Bill is related to the agreement outlined in the joint ministerial Press statement in April 1973 that subject to further consideration of particular aspects, the greater part of the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> business of the Commonwealth Banking Corporation be transferred to a new <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Government commercial bank which is to be established. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731017_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-48-0)

* As the Treasurer  (Mr Crean)  indicated in the paper 'Australia's External Aid 1973-74' which he presented on the occasion of his 1 973-74 Budget Speech, a payment of $ 1 5m will be made to the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Government in 1973-74 to facilitate the establishment of this proposed government commercial bank. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731017_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-48-0)

* I am advised that it is the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Loans Guarantee Bill which is No. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* A condition of the sale of the Commonwealth's interest in Commonwealth New Guinea Timbers Ltd was that upon transfer of the shares to the Investment Corporation the other major shareholder in Commonwealth New Guinea Timbers Ltd - Placer Development Ltd - would arrange an amalgamation of all other wholly owned Placer assets in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> with those of Commonwealth New Guinea Timbers Ltd. To this end an amalgamation agreement with Placer Development Ltd has been endorsed by the board of Commonwealth New Guinea Timbers, with the result that the respective shareholdings in the consolidated company, which will still be known as Common- wealth New Guinea Timbers Ltd, will be held 65 per cent by Placer and 35 per cent by the Investment Corporation. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720822_senate_27_s53/#subdebate-66-0)

* Membership of the bank now totals some 37 countries, 23 of which, including Australia and <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>, are from the Asian region. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720822_senate_27_s53/#subdebate-69-0)

* We praise ourselves for contributing 1 per cent of our gross national product to aid projects today but that sum includes the enormous and very creditable aomunt of money that we are spending in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. * We hope that it will give some consideration to what has been expounded by the Australian Democratic Labor Party for at least 10 years; that is that much of the aid which allegedly we have been granting abroad has been going into the specific responsibility that we have for <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720822_senate_27_s53/#subdebate-69-0)

* But the Democratic Labor Party would like to see the percentage of the gross national product going into international development in our area to be exclusive of the personal responsibility - if one could call it that in referring to a nation - which we in Australia feel towards <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. * Its purpose is to transfer power over lighthouses in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> to the Government of the Territory. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720822_senate_27_s53/#subdebate-70-0)

* We view it as a further step towards self government and the eventual independence of the Territory of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> and its people. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720822_senate_27_s53/#subdebate-70-0)

* We believe that it is of paramount importance that Australia do everything possible to ensure that on achieving independence <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> is a friendly neighbour. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720822_senate_27_s53/#subdebate-70-0)

* The Bill will remove all reference to the Territory of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> from the Lighthouses Act but it is my view that the friendly light to guide the mariner will continue to send out its beam as usual, despite the historic administrative changes taking place in this area. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720829_senate_27_s53/#subdebate-9-0)

* The accident in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> involves 30 people, a large number of whom are cadets, on a Caribou aircraft which is missing on a flight between Lae and Port Moresby. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720829_senate_27_s53/#subdebate-9-0)

* This is the special position of aviation in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720829_senate_27_s53/#subdebate-41-0)

* More than half a million passengers and almost 20,000 tons of freight and mail were carried by airline operators in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> in 1971-72. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720829_senate_27_s53/#subdebate-41-0)

* Air transport and the aeroplane obviously have a vital role in almost every phase of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>'s development. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720829_senate_27_s53/#subdebate-41-0)

* This extensive, safe and efficient aviation industry which now exists in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> is soundly based on the network of aviation facilities and supporting services developed and maintained by the Department of Civil Aviation over many years. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720829_senate_27_s53/#subdebate-41-0)

* It is pleasing to note, therefore, that a Select Transport Committee of the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> House of Assembly has acknowledged that, when <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> becomes independent, it will inherit a more advanced and efficient aviation system than probably any emerging country in the same position. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720829_senate_27_s53/#subdebate-41-0)

* The Government has encouraged the move of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> to self government and eventual independence. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720829_senate_27_s53/#subdebate-41-0)

* I am confident that we can work out with the Chief Minister and his colleagues a programme for the acceptance by the local authorities of responsibility for civil aviation in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720829_senate_27_s53/#subdebate-41-0)

* When I came in from <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> fairly late last night I naturally sought some information on this matter. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720912_senate_27_s53/#subdebate-13-0)

* I ask the Minister for Civil Aviation a question and I refer to the recent joint statement by the Chief Minister of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>, the Minister for Civil Aviation and the Minister for External Territories with regard to the future civil aviation policy in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720912_senate_27_s53/#subdebate-23-0)

* It was stated that it is proposed to offer shareholdings in a single national airline in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> to Ansett Airlines of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>, Trans-Australia Airlines and Qantas Airways Ltd. Is the involvement of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> in the new airline to be totally a government contribution or are shareholdings also to be offered for private investment? [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720912_senate_27_s53/#subdebate-23-0)

* <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> would share in the operation through the Government of their country taking a responsible portion of it. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720912_senate_27_s53/#subdebate-23-0)

* The Australian Labor Party firmly believes that we ought to do in this country what has been done in the United States of America and the United Kingdom and allow our people to vote at 18 years of age as the citizens of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> voted at 18 in the election held earlier this year. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720913_senate_27_s53/#subdebate-49-0)

* Similarly, ordinances made in the Northern Territory, in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> and in other Territories of the Commonwealth over varying periods of years may be inoperative. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720913_senate_27_s53/#subdebate-54-0)

* I present the report of the fifth conference of the Presiding Officers and Clerks of the Parliaments of Australia, Fiji, Nauru, <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> and Western Samoa held in Parliament House, Perth from 16th to 18th May 1972. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720919_senate_27_s53/#debate-45)

* by leave - Honourable senators will recall that, during a statement to the Senate on 29th August outlining recent Government decisions on civil aviation policy, I said that, in the light of early self government and independence, I proposed to visit <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> to discuss a programme for the transfer of civil aviation responsibility to the local authorities. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720919_senate_27_s53/#subdebate-52-0)

* Those discussions between myself and the Chief Minister for <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>,  Mr Somare,  were held in Port Moresby on 3rd, 4th and 5th September and I believe it would be appropriate if I outlined the results to the Senate. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720919_senate_27_s53/#subdebate-52-0)

* A major point to emerge was the strong desire of the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Government to establish a single national airline as soon as possible. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720919_senate_27_s53/#subdebate-52-0)

* Such an airline would become a symbol of the development of national unity within <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720919_senate_27_s53/#subdebate-52-0)

* The <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Government expressed appreciation for the past and present services of the Department of Civil Aviation and the Australian airlines in providing a first class aviation system within and through <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> and indicated that it wanted to utilise their accumulated expertise, experience and many skilled personnel. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720919_senate_27_s53/#subdebate-52-0)

* Mr Somare  said his Government, in addition to its own substantial investment on behalf of its people, wished to offer shareholdings in the new national airline to Trans-Australis Airlines, Ansett Airlines of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> and Qantas Airways Ltd. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720919_senate_27_s53/#subdebate-52-0)

* Discussions will have to be held in the months ahead between the Australian airlines and the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Government on the ways this proposal can be implemented. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720919_senate_27_s53/#subdebate-52-0)

* The <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Government also is obviously mindful of Qantas's record in providing senior managerial staff in the past in Fiji, Singapore, Malaysia and the New Hebrides. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720919_senate_27_s53/#subdebate-52-0)

* It was agreed that the timetable for the establishment of the new airline initially was a matter for the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Government and that, although Australia agreed in principle with the proposal, there was no financial commitment by the Australian Government. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720919_senate_27_s53/#subdebate-52-0)

* The new national airline also will operate services between <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> and Australia when it is able to do so. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720919_senate_27_s53/#subdebate-52-0)

* After <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> becomes independent, Qantas will be the Australian designated international carrier under the air services arrangements which will need to be made between Australia and <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720919_senate_27_s53/#subdebate-52-0)

* The <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Government indicated also that it wants Qantas to continue to provide international air services on its behalf until its own national airline is able to assume this role as well. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720919_senate_27_s53/#subdebate-52-0)

* The second  major area covered in my discussions with  Mr Somare  involved the transfer of the civil aviation functions in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> that are now performed by the Australian Department of Civil Aviation. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720919_senate_27_s53/#subdebate-52-0)

* However, as the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Minister for Transport  Mr B.  R. Jephcott had explained earlier, the local Department of Transport has neither the staff, finance, nor expertise nec essary to consider any large scale involvement in DCA operations in the foreseeable future. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720919_senate_27_s53/#subdebate-52-0)

* Under these circumstances it was agreed that the Australian Department of Civil Aviation will continue to carry out the entire range of civil aviation functions, but that the appropriate local authorities will be fully and continuously consulted on aviation policy matters as they affect <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720919_senate_27_s53/#subdebate-52-0)

* Consideration will be given in the meantime to the machinery which would allow the Department of Civil Aviation to provide, beyond the commencement of full internal self-government, functions of a specialist and operational nature on an agency basis for the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Government. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720919_senate_27_s53/#subdebate-52-0)

* The <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Government indicated it would wish the Department to do this. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720919_senate_27_s53/#subdebate-52-0)

* To assist the consultative processes the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Government has decided to appoint a civil aviation adviser, who will be directly responsible to the appropriate <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Minister. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720919_senate_27_s53/#subdebate-52-0)

* Dr Bradfield  will be under contract to the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Government, and will provide <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> with its own specialist aviation expertise. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720919_senate_27_s53/#subdebate-52-0)

* He is there to be used in the consultative processes between the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> authorities and the Australian authorities. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720919_senate_27_s53/#subdebate-52-0)

* He will also, immediately upon taking up duty, be advising the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Government on all policy aspects. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720919_senate_27_s53/#subdebate-52-0)

* One of his first tasks will be to build up the competence and expertise in the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Public Service to enable it ultimately to take over full responsibility  for  civil aviation. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720919_senate_27_s53/#subdebate-52-0)

* The Department of Civil Aviation does have, and will continue to have, programmes for training Papua New Guineans in various technical and operational functions. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720919_senate_27_s53/#subdebate-52-0)

* In fact the total staff of 1,710 in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> includes 1,160 local officers. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720919_senate_27_s53/#subdebate-52-0)

* Since the early 1960s more than 400 Papua New Guineans have received some formal training provided by the Department - for example, as airport firemen, airways operations officers, administrative staff, artisans and apprentices of various trades. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720919_senate_27_s53/#subdebate-52-0)

* Accordingly, the Department is sponsoring trainees in professional and sub-professional courses at the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Institute of Technology at Lae. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720919_senate_27_s53/#subdebate-52-0)

* Trainees have also been sponsored in the preliminary year of the University of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> preparatory to airways operations training. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720919_senate_27_s53/#subdebate-52-0)

* Therefore it was my very great pleasure while in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> to open a $665,000 civil aviation training college at Taldora, near the Port Moresby airport. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720919_senate_27_s53/#subdebate-52-0)

* The Department has also renewed an offer to train in Australia 2 or 3 selected Papua New Guineans in policy and management functions. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720919_senate_27_s53/#subdebate-52-0)

* However, I believe that the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Ministers whom I met were completely satisfied about the intentions of the Australian Government in respect of transfer of responsibility for civil aviation and the positive steps which we have proposed and which I have just outlined. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720919_senate_27_s53/#subdebate-52-0)

* I was also able to tell the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Ministers about plans to develop the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> airways and ground facilities system. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720919_senate_27_s53/#subdebate-52-0)

* In addition to the decisions I had announced during the previous week to construct a new runway for Port Moresby airport and to develop a new airport for Lae at Nadzab, night flying facilities will be established on selected <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> air routes at a cost of $300,000'. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720919_senate_27_s53/#subdebate-52-0)

* The introduction of night flying facilities will allow greater flexibility in scheduling and provide additional utilisation for aircraft in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720919_senate_27_s53/#subdebate-52-0)

* In my view the visit I paid to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> was most fruitful. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720919_senate_27_s53/#subdebate-52-0)

* My meetings with the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Chief Minister and other Ministers were constructive and cordial. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720919_senate_27_s53/#subdebate-52-0)

* I had too, the benefit of the advice and help of senior officers from the Department of Civil Aviation, External Territories and the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Administration and for this I am truly appreciative also. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720919_senate_27_s53/#subdebate-52-0)

* The only exceptions will be where preferences are accorded on a range of specified items to those Commonwealth countries, such as Canada and New Zealand, with which Australia has bilateral preferential agreements, or where preferences are given to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> or, on a limited range of items, to former or existing dependencies of the United Kingdom. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720920_senate_27_s53/#subdebate-54-0)

* We are already discussing with New Zealand and Canada the question of the future of the preferences they enjoy in Australia, The importance of the preferences accorded to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> and the former or existing British territories is also fully recognised and if, after examination, it appears to the Australian Government that some action is necessary in relation to those preferences, discussions will be held with the particular territories concerned. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720920_senate_27_s53/#subdebate-54-0)

* I ask: Was the statement by  Sir Reginald  Ansett last Friday correct when he claimed that a factor in the purchase of additional 700 series Boeings by both Ansett Airlines of Australia and Trans-Australia Airlines would be for their operation between Australia and <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>? [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720926_senate_27_s54/#subdebate-7-0)

* A part of it would be flying to and from <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720926_senate_27_s54/#subdebate-7-0)

* If the honourable senator were to read carefully the statement which was issued by the Chief Minister of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> and myself, and which was later amplified on in this Parliament, he would find what is proposed for <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> is a joining together for the service of the people of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> of the Ansett activities, the Australian National Airlines Commission activities and the Qantas activities. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720926_senate_27_s54/#subdebate-7-0)

* I ask: ls it a fact that a dispute exists between Australia and <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> over the fixing of a border between the 2 countries? [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720926_senate_27_s54/#subdebate-33-0)

* There have been consultations with regard to the delineation of the boundaries between Australia and <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>, especially having regard to the rather extraordinary boundary that was marked out in former days. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720926_senate_27_s54/#subdebate-33-0)

* My question is directed to either the Minister representing the Minister for External Territories or the Attorney-General, whoever is the more appropriate, or to both of them in their respective capacities, lt concerns the public outcry in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> about telephone tapping and eavesdropping by public officials in connection with the administration of justice and the reports that even the conversations of lawyers with their clients have been telephone tapped, to use the ordinary expression, and that there seems to be no law to prevent this or, if there is, that it is not being enforced. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720926_senate_27_s54/#subdebate-34-0)

* Could either or both of the Ministers inform the Senate of the practice in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> with regard to eavesdropping by public officials or the interception of telephone conversations? * Whether or not such tapping is consistent with the law of the Territory of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> I am unable to say. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720926_senate_27_s54/#subdebate-34-0)

* All I can say is that the Telephonic Communications (Interception) Act which we have in force in Australia does not apply in the Territory of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720926_senate_27_s54/#subdebate-34-0)

[[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720926_senate_27_s54/#subdebate-80-0)

* To date, no formal request has been made by the Japanese Government to establish a consulate in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19721011_senate_27_s54/#subdebate-61-0)

* As announced by the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Chief Minister on 31st August 1972 it has been agreed between Australia and <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Ministers that all proposals for the establishment of consulates in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> would be referred to the Administrator's Executive Council for endorsement before being approved by the Australian Government. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19721011_senate_27_s54/#subdebate-61-0)

* Other reports indicate that the Australian Government made the decision to set up the consortium for the Territory airline without consulting the Government of the Territory of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19721018_senate_27_s54/#subdebate-34-0)

* I ask the Minister whether he will undertake to table in the Senate all documents associated with the Territory of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> airline deal, such documents to include complete reports of any discussions held between officials and Ministers of the 2 governments, in an effort to eliminate the bad feeling now obviously existing in the Territory. * The suggested transfer of islands in Torres Strait from the sovereignty of the State of Queensland and/or the Commonwealth of Australia to the emerging independent nation of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730228_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-60-0)

* to this question of the proposed transfer of the sovereignty of part of Queensland, part of the Commonwealth of Australia, to the emerging nation of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>, to lay down certain propositions and particularly that the people of the Torres Strait islands, the area concerned, must be consulted. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730228_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-60-0)

* We are dealing with a group of islands that lie between Cape York Peninsula and Papua, which is part of the Territory of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730228_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-60-0)

* The original proposal by the Commonwealth Government was that the boundary should be realigned and that 3 of those islands - Saibai, Boigu and Dauan - should be transferred to the Territory of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> which will soon be an independent nation quite foreign to Australia. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730228_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-60-0)

* Then there was a transposition of that original proposal which said that the line should even be dropped further south of the 10th parallel, that that should be the demarcation line and that all the islands north of that should pass from the sovereignty of the State of Queensland and/ or the sovereignty of the Commonwealth of Australia to the sovereignty of the emerging nation of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730228_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-60-0)

* If the truncation were to take place merely to separate these 3 islands to which I have referred and to put them in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> that would be bad, but to drop the demarcation line down to the 10th parallel and take probably 4,000 or 5,000 of the Torres Strait islanders out of the sovereignty of Australia and Queensland and transfer them to the sovereignty of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> is virtually the complete destruction of a nation. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730228_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-60-0)

* It is a monstrous suggestion, and it would be even more monstrous to permit this total ethnic group - virtually this , total nation - to be cut in 2, severed, and part of it willy-nilly transferred to the Territory of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730228_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-60-0)

* I do not know - and nobody knows - how the new emerging nation of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> will operate. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730228_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-60-0)

* There is a position which opens the possibility, looking at the matter in the constitutional framework, that the Commonwealth Parliament with Her Majesty in Council - whether that would be Her Majesty in the Executive Council of Australia or in the Privy Council in England - could unilaterally and without consulting anybody whatsoever transfer these territories to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730228_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-60-0)

* In a joint statement issued by the Prime Minister and  Mr Somare,  the Chief Minister of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>, on 17th January last this appears: [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730228_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-60-0)

* There is the obvious and proclaimed intention and attitude of the Prime Minister in conjunction with that of the Chief Minister of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> that they think the boundary should be relocated. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730228_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-60-0)

* They have said: Well, when <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> emerges into independence we want to have good relations with that country'. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730228_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-60-0)

* The only substantial sea passage around the northern tip of Australia lies through the great north east passage between some of these islands and the shoreline of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730228_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-60-0)

* If the border is brought down to the tenth parallel, 14 islands will be transferred to the emerging nation of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730228_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-60-0)

* There has been merely the vague statement that this course would make for good relations for <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730228_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-60-0)

* I say this to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>: The people of the Torres Strait Islands belong to a different ethnic group. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730228_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-60-0)

* Action could be taken then to exclude them from <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> and put them somewhere else but these people cannot lightly be dispersed. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730228_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-60-0)

* They could not be placed in some place in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730228_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-60-0)

* Senator Byrne  handled the whole of this debate as though the Australian Government wanted to excise some islands on which certain people lived and to give those islands to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730228_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-62-0)

* He did not say that the border was several miles out to sea from Queensland and but one mile from <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730228_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-62-0)

* But he, above all, knows perfectly well that in a very short time this will not be a matter of States but a matter of a border between an independent, sovereign country - that is <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> on the one hand and Australia on the other. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730228_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-62-0)

* The preamble to the motion appears to assert that the issues involved in negotiations concerning the border between Australia and <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> are matters for the Queensland Parliament. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730228_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-62-0)

* The motion implies that the matter of the border between Australia and <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> affects the Torres Strait islanders alone. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730228_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-62-0)

* The fact is that all citizens of Australia are affected by the border problem with a neighbouring country and the interests of the people of Australia and <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> as a whole must be considered in any settlement which is reached. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730228_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-62-0)

* The first and most fundamental desire for this settlement is that the Government is anxious to remove a source of possible friction between an independent <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> and Australia. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730228_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-62-0)

* Secondly, the maintenance of an Australian border within a few hundred metres of the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> shoreline would be quite untenable internationally. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730228_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-62-0)

* It was set while Australia was still a British colony and was made, of course, without consultation of the Australian people as a whole or, indeed, the people of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730228_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-62-0)

* I take this opportunity to point out to honourable senators that the wishes and rights of the people inhabiting these islands have been at the forefront of consideration of this matter by this Government and the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Government. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730228_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-62-0)

* I quote the following passage from a communique issued by the Prime Minister  (Mr Whitiam)  and the Chief Minister of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> on 17th January this year as evidence of this attitude. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730228_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-62-0)

* The Australian Government would facilitate contact between the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Government and the islanders if the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Government wishes. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730228_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-62-0)

* The Prime Minister and the Chief Minister agreed that Australian officials should engage in early discussions with <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> officials with a view to seeking provisional agreement between Australia and <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> on issues other than that of territorial sovereignty of the islands. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730228_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-62-0)

* An interdepartmental committee of interested Commonwealth departments at this moment is giving consideration to attitudes to be taken by the Commonwealth in the proposed discussions with <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> officials. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730228_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-62-0)

* The attitude of the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Government was expressed in another way by  Mr Ebia  Olewale, who is Minister for Education, in a statement reported on 3rd May 1972 in which he said that it was unreasonable to ask <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> to put up with a situation which Queensland would not tolerate should the positions be reversed. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730228_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-62-0)

* The crux of the matter is that the Commonwealth Government has recognised that the present border between <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> and Australia is in need of adjustment, and having recognised that fact the Government is anxious to arrange a settlement which is in the best interests of all the parties concerned. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730228_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-62-0)

* On the other hand  Mr Bjelke-Petersen  apparently believes that the border should not be changed under any circumstances and that it represents a perfectly acceptable situation for the present border to run so close to the coast of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730228_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-62-0)

* I believe that  Mr Olewale's  comment is relevant here and that  Mr Bjelke-Petersen  should try to place himself in the New Guineans' position in order to see that <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> has a reasonable case for requesting a variation of the present border. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730228_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-62-0)

* Given this assurance, I underline the point that if this motion is carried and  Senator Byrne's  view, as wrong as it is, is given credence, it could only inhibit future negotiations between 2 sovereign nations - <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> on the one hand and Australia on the other. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730228_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-62-0)

* We have said that we appreciate the situation that <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> places before us. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730228_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-62-0)

* <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> becomes independent. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730228_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-62-0)

* It has been stated time and time again that whatever negotiations take place the people will count with the Australian and the Papua New Guinean governments. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730228_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-62-0)

* Finally, I repeat that the issue is not a question of what the situation is tonight because in a very short space of time the Queensland Government will not have responsibility for this matter; it will be the responsibility of a properly elected government of Australia dealing with an independent <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> which will be relying on us in all sorts of ways. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730228_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-62-0)

* <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> has a right to expect that the country which has been a colonial power over these years - quite unwillingly on our part - should be looking towards it to help it to great nationhood. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730228_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-62-0)

* We are co-operating with <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> on a wide variety of fronts, such as allowing it into international conferences to speak in its own right, by making special considerations for it, setting up organisations for it, discussing where we can help in the field of foreign relations, where we can represent it and where it should represent itself. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730228_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-62-0)

* I ask the members of the Senate tonight to think very carefully about the vote they are about to make because the result could very easily inhibit a future government in Australia, whatever its political colour and whatever might be the situation in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> at that time. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730228_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-62-0)

* It reads:  1 am writing to you because one of my constituents has asked me to support the transfer of your island to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730228_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-62-0)

* I do not believe that <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> has any right to your land but I wouldlike to hear from you about it. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730228_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-62-0)

* I am writing to you now because when I received the letter setting out the claim to your wishes  1  realised that some people in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> have started a campaign which may be difficult to stop unless the people of the islands speak now with the help of their friends on the Australian mainland. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730228_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-62-0)

* With all their movements around the islands, the film crew could not find one person who wanted to give those islands to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730228_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-62-0)

* I should like to quote also from an article in the November 1972-January 1973 issue of Australia's Neighbours' entitled 'The Boundary Between Australia and <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>'. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730228_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-62-0)

* the present boundary is a' perfectly proper boundary in the terms of the existing Convention, unless some historic title or other special circumstances can be demonstrated by the Government of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> and accepted by Australia. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730228_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-62-0)

* If we're going to be given away to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>, our race will die out,'  Mr Getano  Lui said in Brisbane yesterday. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730228_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-62-0)

* What has happened in the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> House of Assembly on this question? [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730228_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-62-0)

* If the boundary is moved then <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>, having independence, would have no hesitation in drilling for oil in the Torres Strait. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730228_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-62-0)

* the border dispute arose from a claim by  Mr Somare,  <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Chief Minister, that because the islands were close to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> they should belong to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730228_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-62-0)

* 
 Mr Somare also said <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> wanted fishing rights. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730228_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-62-0)

* I also criticise  Senator Bonner  for saying: If you take these 3 islands out and put them into the Territory of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> you will take away unemployment benefits.' [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730228_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-62-0)

* They hope that they will divide the people of Queensland and the island people and cause trouble between the people of the Territory of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> and the people who live on the islands in Torres Strait. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730228_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-62-0)

* Probably under the guidance and leadership of the Chief Minister of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>,  Mr Michael  Somare, our own representatives and the people in the areas concerned, an agreement will be hammered out which will be acceptable to all. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730228_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-62-0)

* Members of the Labor Party seem to be quite happy to hand over to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> 3 islands in the Torres Strait. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730228_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-62-0)

* The issue has been discussed between the chief Minister of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>,  Mr Somare,  and the Prime Minister,  Mr Whitlam. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730228_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-62-0)

* Now there is a possibility that they will become Papua New Guineans because someone down here is to say: 'You are not going to be. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730228_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-62-0)

* We are going to give away your nationality and give you to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>.' [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730228_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-62-0)

* You are, because if you give these islands to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> the islanders will not remain there. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730228_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-62-0)

* J ask that they be given an opportunity to say to the Government or to the representatives of the Government whether they want to be Papua New Guineans. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730228_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-62-0)

* 1 have heard many silly arguments here tonight about the islands being too close to the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> border. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730228_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-62-0)

* What about the bolder between West Irian and <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>? [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730228_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-62-0)

* Some people say that because the islands are too close to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> we should give them to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730228_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-62-0)

* What difference does it make if the islands are a mile or 2 yards away from <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>? [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730228_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-62-0)

* So because we want to save the people of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>, bless them, from going an extra mile, it is suggested that we should give 570-odd people to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> when they do not want to become part of that country. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730228_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-62-0)

* I say that we should not give part of Queensland to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730228_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-62-0)

* May I remind  Senator Bonner  of his brothers and sisters in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730228_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-62-0)

* For some reason he seemed to separate them from his brothers and sisters - he used the term - in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730228_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-62-0)

* 1 would like to remind him that <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> is an emerging nation with a tremendous potential for growth, commercially and otherwise, and it will not be long before the interests of the Torres Strait islanders will be better served by the nations to the north of them than by the State to the south of them. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730228_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-62-0)

* He had the temerity to use the word genocide' because it has been suggested that these 3 islands should become part of the Territory of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730228_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-62-0)

* That is what can be termed genocide, not the relocation, by arrangement and discussion, of a boundary between <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> and Queensland. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730228_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-62-0)

* That boundary is accepted generally today by the politicians of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730228_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-62-0)

* By bringing the border further south, <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> takes in the 3 islands concerned. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730228_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-62-0)

* As far as the negotiations have gone, at the present time the politicians of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> are prepared to accept this boundary which will bring within their territory the 3 islands under discussion. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730228_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-62-0)

* But under the pressure of  Mr Bjelke-Petersen,  the Democratic Labor Party and misguided senators here tonight, this problem will not be resolved until <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> takes it to the International Court of Justice. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730228_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-62-0)

* If it were not for the social services which the Commonwealth provides, those people would be as destitute as the people who live on the mainland of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730228_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-62-0)

* It should not be forgotten that the whole area of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>, the Torres Strait Islands and West Irian, which, incidentally, was created because of the ineptitude of the previous government, which was prepared to concede to Indonesia certain benefits which it ought to have resisted conceding and which has moved the autonomy of that area further away, is the cradle of a new emergent nation and we should not do anything that is likely to stir or to create division. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730228_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-62-0)

* All we are suggesting is that careful and unemotional negotiations should be conducted with the people of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> to reconcile the matter. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730228_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-62-0)

* The people of these islands are of entirely different character, racial background and culture from that of the people of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730228_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-62-0)

* What will happen to the culture of the Torres Strait islanders if the border is changed and these islands come under the jurisdiction of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>? [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730228_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-62-0)

* The position in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> is such at present that nobody in this chamber will be prepared to guarantee the safety of any section of the people of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> when that country receives self-determination Nobody can guarantee th at there will not be some day one of the greatest blood baths in the world in that country. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730228_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-62-0)

* These Torres Strait islanders have no ti;s with the people of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730228_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-62-0)

* They just happen to live adjacent to the coastline of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730228_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-62-0)

* <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> is a country which has nothing to do with them. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730228_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-62-0)

* It has been said that people travelling from one part of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> to another might have to sail through Australian waters. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730228_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-62-0)

* Is there any reason why the lands and homes of the Torres Strait islanders should be ceded to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>? [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730228_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-62-0)

* Cocoa is, of course, a very important commodity to a number of developing countries', particularly ' African countries, and also to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730410_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-46-0)

* <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>'s position as a producer and exporter of significant tonnages of cocoa has, of course, been a paramount consideration in Australia's participation in the negotiation of this Agreement. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730410_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-46-0)

* Cocoa accounts for about 20 per cent of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>'s exports and it is its third most important export commodity. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730410_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-46-0)

* <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> exported some 30,000 tonnes of raw cocoa in the 1971-72 cocoa year, which represented about 2 per cent of world exports. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730410_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-46-0)

* The future of the cocoa industry is of major importance to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> and, indeed, on the basis of the country's overall development program, it could well become an increasingly important agricultural export commodity within the short space of a few years. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730410_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-46-0)

* Hence <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> has a very real interest in obtaining stable and remunerative prices for its cocoa while at the same time having the opportunity to plan ahead its production program on a sound and predictable basis. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730410_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-46-0)

* In this connection, it was possible to negotiate export control provisions which in effect mean that <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>'s aspirations should be adequately accommodated within the Agreement, lt was determined that some 75 per cent of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>'s exports is of a type of cocoa which is exempted from export controls, while the remaining 25 per cent will not be subject to controls at present because of the small quantity involved. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730410_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-46-0)

[[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730410_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-46-0)

* Following independence, the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Government will need to consider the question of separate membership in the Agreement. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730410_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-46-0)

[[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730410_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-46-0)

* It is a comprehensive Bill designed to abolish the death penalty for all purposes under Commonwealth law and under the law of all Territories other than <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730410_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-63-0)

* This Bill seeks the approval of Parliament to the provision of a guarantee by the Commonwealth for a borrowing in various currencies equivalent to$US9.8m -$A6.9m - by the Administration of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> from the Asian Development Bank. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730411_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-54-0)

* The proceeds of the loan will assist in financing a highways project in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730411_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-54-0)

* The Highlands Highway between Lae and Goroka was completed as a gravel surfaced road in 1965 and is the only access road to the Highlands area which contains almost half the total population of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730411_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-54-0)

* The loan is the second which the Asian Development Bank has made to the Administration since the admission of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> to membership of the Bank in April 1971. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730411_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-54-0)

* The first loan of$US4.5m was for relending to the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Development Bank and the Commonwealth guarantee for that loan was approved by the Papau New Guinea Loan (Asian Development Bank) Act 1972. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730411_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-54-0)

* Borrowings by the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Administration automatically carry a Commonwealth guarantee by virtue of the operation of section 75a of the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Act 1949-1971. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730411_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-54-0)

* In practice, however, this provision is usually supplemented in some way for borrowings other than those in Australia and <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730411_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-54-0)

* I would mention that at the time of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>'s admission to the Asian Development Bank Australia gave an undertaking to the Bank in accordance with Article 3.3 of the agreement establishing the Bank that, until <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> itself assumes responsibility for its own international relations, Australia would be responsible for all obligations that may be incurred by <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> by reason of its admission to membership in the Bank and enjoyment of the benefits of such membership. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730411_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-54-0)

* In addition to guaranteeing the repayment of principal and payment of interest and other charges on the loan until such time as <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> assumes responsibility for its own international relations, the letter gives certain other customary assurances required by the Bank. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730411_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-54-0)

* Because these assurances go further than the statutory guarantee already provided under section 75a of the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Act it is necessary for specific Commonwealth legislation to be passed in order for the assurances to constitute valid and binding obligations of the Commonwealth as required by the Bank. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730411_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-54-0)
