* The general proposition as outlined in  Mr Chan's  comments is that <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> will be a responsible country in the economic and financial sense and will encourage investment of capital in that country for sensible purposes. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730412_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-43-0)

* I would mention that at the time of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>'s admission to the Asian Development Bank Australia gave an undertaking to the Bank in accordance with Article 3.3 of the agreement establishing the Bank that, until <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> itself assumes responsibility for its own international relations, Australia would be responsible for all obligations that may be incurred by <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> by reason of its admission to membership in the Bank and enjoyment of the benefits of such membership. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730412_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-43-0)

* That statement predicates the contemplated situation that when <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> assumes political independence a new relationship will develop between Australia and that country in which that country will e considered to be on its own and free from the solicitude, regard and attention that are now being devoted to it by Australia. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730412_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-43-0)

* While <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> may well achieve political independence very quickly, it will by -no means have achieved economic independence or even complete economic viability. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730412_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-43-0)

* Therefore, the Government of this country should still contemplate the fact that, if <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> in its present position of what we may call dependence receives guarantees from Australia for the Asian Development Bank to support its loan indebtedness, no vastly different position should be allowed to obtain merely with its emergence into independence. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730412_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-43-0)

* Then the position of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> politically, socially and economically could be really bad. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730412_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-43-0)

* We trust that this support, which in this case will improve transportation in one of the areas of the world in which transportation at a high level can be of the very greatest significance, will help to build a transport system through the whole of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> so that, with that as a base, economic improvement and expansion can come all the more quickly, readily and effectively to the emerging independent nation of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730412_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-43-0)

*  I would like to take some small part in the debate on the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Loan (Asian Development Bank) Bill in order to support it and the remarks made by  Senator Cotton. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730412_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-43-0)

* The details of the measure have been outlined and referred to already, lt is well known that its purpose is to finance a highway project that is designed to serve a region that contains approximately half the population of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730412_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-43-0)

* As honourable senators probably know, the initiation of projects for international loan proposals falls within the authority of the responsible Minister in the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Government, and the Commonwealth Government formally guarantees such loans from international agencies. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730412_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-43-0)

* <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> became a member of the Asian Development Bank in 1971. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730412_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-43-0)

* <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> is, of course, of vital importance not only to its future economic and social development but also in assisting to bring about a greater sense of what I will call political unity. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730412_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-43-0)

* <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> is a country of considerable ethnic diversity, and any serious obstacles to communication will be a hindrance to the development of independence. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730412_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-43-0)

* I am interested in the speech made by the Chief Minister of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>,  Mr Somare,  during the visit of the Australian Prime Minister  (Mr Whitlam)  earlier this year. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730412_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-43-0)

* I think that  Mr Somare  was acknowledging in those words the interdependence that countries such as Australia and <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> have in the total area of the international aid program. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730412_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-43-0)

* This is the case with <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730412_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-43-0)

* It is true to say that we have a special responsibility as independence approaches in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730412_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-43-0)

* I think that after <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> attains independence Australia will assume with it an aid relationship which is similar to those which Australia has at present with other countries. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730412_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-43-0)

* In the current financial year our estimated expenditure on external aid amounts to $220m, of which S145m or almost two-thirds goes in various forms of aid to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730412_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-43-0)

* I do not want to take the discussion on international aid any further than that at this stage because the Bill deals primarily with the activities of the Asian Development Bank, of which Australia is a member and through which it extends assistance to a large number of countries, in particular <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730412_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-43-0)

* The Bill gives us a relationship to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730412_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-43-0)

* Emphasis is placed on our role through the Bank and on the important field of assistance to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> to enable it to become not only a worthy nation in the family of nations but also a very friendly and acceptable neighbour. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730412_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-43-0)

* I appreciate the speedy passage of the Bill and the sympathetic remarks which were made by  Senator Cotton, Senator Drake-Brockman, Senator Byrne  and  Senator Davidson  about the great problems confronting the people of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730412_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-43-0)

* In his speech the Governor-General referred to the creation of an independent united <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730501_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-76-0)

* Since 2nd December and, more particularly, since the appointment of the Minister for External Territories, there has been a continuing process  of  giving  to  <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> the indepen dence for which it so bravely worked over so many years. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730501_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-76-0)

* By the end of this year there will be very little control by the Australian Government over the affairs of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730501_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-76-0)

* What was the cost of the aircraft chartered by the Australian Government to take the Prime Minister and his party to the Territory of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> and Indonesia and return. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730501_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-90-0)

* The net cost to the Australian Government in respect of the aircraft chartered to take the Prime Minister and his party to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> and Indonesiais expected to be $18,300. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730501_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-90-0)

* There is constant communication between all who are interested in the new boundaries between <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> and Australia. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730502_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-17-0)

* In view of the fact that the Prime Minister has seen fit to confer with the Chief Minister for <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>,  Mr Somare,  on the Torres Strait Islands border issue, and considering the statement attributed to the Minister for Aboriginal Affairs recently in the Press, has the Prime Minister taken any steps to confer with -the leaders of the Torres Strait Islands people and the Queensland Government on a matter which is of great importance in the lives of many Australian citizens? [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730502_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-32-0)

* The purpose of this Bill is to abolish the death penalty from the laws under the jurisdiction of the Australian Parliament, except those of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730503_senate_28_s55/#subdebate-60-0)

*  Mr President,  I would like to present a statement on the constitutional development of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730508_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-44-0)

* Its aim is to abolish the death penalty from all Commonwealth law except that applicable to the Territory of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730508_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-53-0)

* As a nation <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> will need large injections of overseas investments, and the Japanese have plenty of them. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730515_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-35-0)

* The fact of their taking an interest  - I  have not seen it but  I  accept that a report has been made - would not surprise me because it would be in line with the general attitude of their investment in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730515_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-35-0)

* It creates news for the media when somebody in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> says: 'We are not ready, we are being forced into it' and so on. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730515_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-35-0)

* This Bill seeks the approval  of  Parliament to the provision of a contractual guarantee by the Australian Government for an overseas borrowing by <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> in foreign currencies not exceeding the equivalent of $US20m or $A14.3m. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730517_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-42-0)

* Legislation to  authorise  the borrowing, to be used by the Government of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> to finance public works and services, has already been passed by the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> House of Assembly and it is expected that arrangements for the borrowing for which this Bill provides a guarantee will be concluded before the end of this financial year. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730517_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-42-0)

* The borrowing will be the first loan raised by <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> on international capital markets, although this is not the first time Parliament has been asked to approve the provision  of  contractual guarantees for overseas borrowings by <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730517_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-42-0)

* Parliament has on several previous occasions approved such guarantees by the Australian Government in respect of loans to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> from the International Bank for Reconstruction and Development and the Asian Development Bank. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730517_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-42-0)

* All borrowings by <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> internally or on the Australian market, or course, carry  a  statutory guarantee by the Australian Government by virtue of section 75a of the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Act. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730517_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-42-0)

* One of the loan possibilities currently being investigated by the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Government is a public bond issue denominated in deutschemarks underwritten by  an  international syndicate of banking and financial institutions, which makes it necessary to seek parliamentary approval for the provision of the guarantee in advance of the time the issue is actually negotiated. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730517_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-42-0)

* There would, therefore, be insufficient time to seek parliamentary approval for the guarantee after the loan agreement has been signed,  as  has been the normal practice with guarantees for loans to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> by the International Bank for Reconstruction and Development and the Asian Development Bank. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730517_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-42-0)

* The form of guarantee that is customarily required in international capital markets is similar to those that have been given to the International Bank for Reconstruction and Development and to the Asian Development Bank in respect of borrowings by <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> from those institutions. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730517_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-42-0)

* The Bill is purposely couched  in  general terms in respect of the currency and the precise form of the proposed borrowing so as not to restrict <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>'s choice as to the particular overseas market  in  which it finally decided to arrange the loan. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730517_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-42-0)

* In present circumstances, it seems probable that the cost of  an  overseas borrowing by <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> will not differ greatly from the cost of a borrowing for a comparable term from institutional sources in Australia. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730517_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-42-0)

* The <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Government wishes to undertake  an  overseas borrowing as soon as possible to establish a favourable standing in international capital markets before it becomes independent, as this could enhance its borrowing prospects thereafter. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730517_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-42-0)

* A contractual guarantee by the Australian Government for such a borrowing should ensure the success of this first issue and will materially assist <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> in furthering this longer term objective. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730517_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-42-0)

* The 1971 agreement, which was signed on 18th May 1971, delimits the seabed between Australia and Indonesia in the Arafura Sea and between <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> and Indonesia off the southern and northern coasts of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730517_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-47-0)

* The boundaries relating to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> were approved in 1971 by the Administrator's Executive Council. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730517_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-47-0)

* The 1973 agreement, which was signed on 12th February 1973 by the Chief Minister of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>,  Mr Somare,  one behalf of the Australian Government, deals with the land boundary of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>, and with the seabed boundary immediately south of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730517_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-47-0)

* The 1973 agreement provides in addition that the seabed boundary lines shall also serve, so rar as necessary, as the lateral boundaries of the territorial seas and exclusive fishing zones of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> and Indonesia. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730517_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-47-0)

* The 1973 agreement has been approved by the Administrator's Executive Council of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730517_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-47-0)

* ment expressly envisages that the approval of the agreement by the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> House of Assembly is to be obtained before Australian ratification of the agreement takes place. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730517_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-47-0)

* The seabed boundaries set out in the 3 agreements differ in some respects from the limits of Australian and <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> adjacent areas' described in the Schedules to the Petroleum (Submerged Lands) Act. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730517_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-47-0)

* In the case of Papua NewGuinea, there is a net gain to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> in the seabed area to the south, while in the north some re-adjustment in favour of Indonesia is required. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730517_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-47-0)

* Passage of this amending legislation will allow the Government to ratify the 1971 and 1972 agreements with Indonesia and ratification of the third agreement will follow, subject to the approval of that agreement by the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> House of Assembly. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730517_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-47-0)

* We now have a boundary which extends from an area north of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> through the Arafura and Timor seas to a point north-west of Aus tralia, incomplete only in the area opposite Portuguese Timor. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730517_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-47-0)

* Fifth, Australia has a very special responsibility for <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> which will soon be self-governing and independent. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730517_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-51-0)

* It is important, therefore, that Australia should leave <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> with industrial laws which accord with international standards. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730517_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-51-0)

* There are several conventions of particular significance for <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> which can only be extended lo <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> and our other non-metropolitan territories when they have been ratified in respect of Australia itself. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730517_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-51-0)

* The ratification of a number of ILO conventions was discussed with the States - at Ministerial level at the meeting of Commonwealth and State Labour Ministers in February and at Permanent Head level at the meeting of the Departments of Labour Advisory Committee held in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> in April. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730517_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-51-0)

* Thus the Government is consulting with the Government of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> to clear up outstanding action required in respect of ILO conventions ratified by Australia. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730517_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-51-0)

* For the first time a tripartite observer delegation from <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> will be attending this year's session of the International Labour Conference and the Minister for Labour anticipates that in company with the Minister for Labour of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> and the other members of the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> delegation he will be able to register with the Director-General of the ILO a considerable number of declarations on ILO conventions for <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730517_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-51-0)

* This Bill seeks the approval of Parliament to provide a contractual guarantee by the Australian Government for an overseas borrowing by <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730522_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-48-0)

* The <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Government, in its emergent state, proposes to undertake an overseas borrowing, whereas in previous years it has depended upon the resources being provided to it either by what I might call grants in aid, revenue grants or subsistence in loan form from the Australian Government which, for a period of time, has been its guardian or trustee. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730522_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-48-0)

* I think that the Australian people, through a variety of governments and a variety of political philosophies, have a great deal to be proud of for the the record which they have achieved in connection with the emergent nation of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> under trusteeship, under guardianship or under custodianship - call it what you will. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730522_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-48-0)

* What is happening in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> is this: The overseas borrowing is being contracted by the emergent nation under a kind of custodianship by the Australian Government and it will be successful not because of the reputation of the emergent nation but because of the reputation of the parent, custodian or guardian and because of the guarantee by that guardian. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730522_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-48-0)

* The proceeds of the loan will be made available to finance public works and services in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730522_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-48-0)

* The legislation to authorise the borrowing has already been passed by the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> House of Assembly. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730522_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-48-0)

* It will be the first loan raised by <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> on the international capital market, but it is not the first time that we, as a parliament, have been asked to approve borrowings by <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730522_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-48-0)

* To the Treasurer  (Mr Crean)  I must pay a personal compliment and say that he responded to ray queries about the currency situation when the Senate was debating the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Loan (Asian Development Bank) Bill. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730522_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-48-0)

* He sent me an explanation of the relative positions of the currency of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> as it is now and what it might be in the future that was quite satisfactory to me. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730522_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-48-0)

* Borrowings by <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> internally or on the Australian market carry a statutory guarantee. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730522_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-48-0)

* <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> is investigating the possibility of raising its loan in deutsche marks. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730522_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-48-0)

* One would understand that perhaps the thing to be considered here is that <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> needs to have implicit in its negotiations the understanding that Australia will underwrite it. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730522_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-48-0)

* Therefore I think the Senate is properly entitled, in accordance with past practice, to give <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> that implicit understanding as it proceeds towards finalising the negotiations, particularly on an overseas market in a part of the world which is .new to it. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730522_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-48-0)

* The comment has been made that the Bill is purposely couched in general terms in respect of the currency and the precise format of the proposed borrowing, that it- is done so as not to restrict the choice of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> in borrowing on a particular overseas capital market from which it may finally decide to arrange its loan. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730522_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-48-0)

* The comment was that in present circumstances it seems probable that the cost of overseas borrowing by <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> will not differ greatly from the cost of borrowing a comparable term loan from an institutional source in Australia. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730522_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-48-0)

* 1  am delighted to hear that <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> will not have to pay more interest on the money that it borrows than it would have to pay if the money were borrowed from a normal Australian source which may have some bond with <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730522_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-48-0)

* If that is the case, I think that to some extent it is probably due to the fact that <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> has an Australian guarantee and an Australian underwriting. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730522_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-48-0)

* One would wish <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> to have that guarantee and underwriting so that it can obtain the lowest effective rate of interest possible in the international capital markets. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730522_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-48-0)

* The point has been made - I think it is a good point - that <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> needs to establish its standing as a borrower in the international capital market. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730522_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-48-0)

* That view seems to me to be quite sensible and I believe that <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> should be supported in that respect. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730522_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-48-0)

* In establishing itself as a borrower <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> will depend upon the quality of its guarantor. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730522_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-48-0)

* Legislation authorising that has already been passed by the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> House of Assembly. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730522_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-48-0)

* It is likely that by the end of this financial year <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> will receive a deutsche mark loan on which the interest rate is not higher than the rate at which a loan would be available from an Australian source. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730522_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-48-0)

* could regard the Australian capital situation today as being of such magnitude, due to the wise and efficient operations of the economy by the previous Government, that the Government could permit a capital loan to be made to the Government of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730522_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-48-0)

* But <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> has alternative ways of obtaining money. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730522_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-48-0)

* For the reasons I have mentioned <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> needs to establish itself internationally as a borrower. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730522_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-48-0)

* <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> is a nation which is emerging towards not only political independence but also, to a large measure, economic and social independence. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730522_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-48-0)

* This measure will provide ongoing finance to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> in its present state and the contractual implications will continue with the new <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> in its independent situation. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730522_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-48-0)

* Also I would be interested to know what will be the future policy of Australia in relation to further finance being made available to the independent nation of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730522_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-48-0)

* I would like to know whether this Bill is to be the first of a series of ongoing financial provisions of a particular kind so that Australia may persist in its solicitude for <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>, or whether it will be the last provision of this character to be made available, after which <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> will be internationally a nation that can go on to the world market and secure its own loans. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730522_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-48-0)

* When 1 speak of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> having political, financial and economic independence I do so in a theoretical sense. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730522_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-48-0)

* Will Australia still act in some condition of patrimony towards <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>? [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730522_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-48-0)

* It is important for <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> to know the answers to those questions and for this Parliament to know them. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730522_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-48-0)

* For that reason I would be obliged if the Minister, in his reply, will indicate what is to be the future financial relationship between the emerging nation of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> and Australia. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730522_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-48-0)

* The purpose of this legislation is to give effect to a series of decisions reached jointly with the Government of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730523_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-38-0)

* These are to transfer responsibility for the Public Service and for auditing the accounts of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> to local executive authority, to implement the recommendations of a report on the future of overseas officers in the Public Service and to make minor amendments to the description of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> in conformity with the terms of the border agreement between Australia and Indonesia signed in February 1973. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730523_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-38-0)

* One is to amend the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Act. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730523_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-38-0)

* Firstly, they will remove the power of the Minister for External Territories under section 30 to appoint officers and engage persons on contract for the Public Service, thus enabling <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> to legislate to develop its own national public service - an essential authority for a country approaching full selfgovernment and independence. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730523_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-38-0)

* This section will be superfluous with the passage of the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> (Staffing Assistance) Bill, to which I will refer later. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730523_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-38-0)

* Thirdly, the amendments provide for the cessation of Australian responsibility for auditing the accounts of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730523_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-38-0)

* This will retain authority for the Australian Auditor-General to complete his final audit, and enable the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Auditor to commence his responsibilities at the beginning of an appropriate financial period. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730523_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-38-0)

* The amendments to the descriptions of the Territories of Papua and of New Guinea are in accordance with the Agreement, concluded with the concurrence of the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Administrator's Executive Council and signed on behalf of Australia by the Chief Minister of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730523_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-38-0)

* I now turn to the Bill entitled the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> (Staffing Assistance) Bill. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730523_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-38-0)

* This Bill is complementary to the proposed amendments to the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Act and is designed, to come into operation on the date on which responsibility for the Public Service is transferred to the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Government. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730523_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-38-0)

* At the present time there are some  5,000  permanent and contract overseas officers of the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Public Service and the Police Force who were appointed as permanent officers or engaged on contract by the Minister for External Territories. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730523_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-38-0)

* The <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Government has indicated that it wants to retain the services of many of these officers and that it sees a continuing need for staff from Australia for some years beyond independence. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730523_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-38-0)

* The Aus tralian Government has given an undertaking to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> that the help of Australians will be available for as long as that help is needed and desired. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730523_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-38-0)

* The <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> (Staffing Assistance) Bill provides the framework under which this may be accomplished and gives effect to the recommendations of a report on the future employment security of overseas officers in the Public Service. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730523_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-38-0)

* His  report was accepted in principle by both the Australian, and <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Governments and was published. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730523_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-38-0)

* <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> (Staffing Assistance). [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730523_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-38-0)

* Bill, in giving effect to the Simpson recommendations, reflects a decision taken jointly by <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> and the former Australian Government and endorsed by the present .Government. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730523_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-38-0)

* Its provisions will result in major changes to the: existing framework under which the Australian Government provides staff for <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730523_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-38-0)

* Under the Bill permanent and contract overseas officers and temporary overseas employee superannuation fund contributors in the Public Service and the Police Force, and staff of the Electricity Commission of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> who are superannuation contributors, will be separated from their respective <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> services and will become part of an Australian staffing assistance group. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730523_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-38-0)

* The persons in this group will not be members of the national Public Service of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> and they will not compete with local officers for promotion within that Service. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730523_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-38-0)

* They will however be made available to occupy and carry out the duties of established positions in the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> national public service and in other areas of public employment until there are Papua New Guineans available to fill these positions and their services are no longer required. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730523_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-38-0)

* <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> and for the period of that service they will form part of the Australian staffing assistance group. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730523_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-38-0)

* Similarly, staff seconded from other areas of Australian public employment will also serve in the group in line with Australia's undertaking to provide continued staffing assistance to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730523_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-38-0)

* Removal of these matters from <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> legislation and their prescription under Australian legislation will meet the assurances given to these officers by the Australian Government that their terms and conditions of service would not be altered without the consent of the Australian Government. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730523_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-38-0)

* A scheme of compensation for premature termination of contracts of employment made by the Minister under the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Act will also be introduced. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730523_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-38-0)

* Pending the introduction of regulations prescribing terms and conditions of employment it provides for the continuation of the relevant provisions of appropriate <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> ordinances and the regulations and determinations made thereunder. * In addition, it provides for the other activities on which there is agreement that TAA should have full powers, namely: (a) aerial work operations; (b) the operation of hotels and other forms of accommodation; (c) joint operations with other carriers; (d) air transport operations in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>, after that country becomes independent, under arrangements which are agreed between the Commonwealth and the Government of that country; and (e) engineering services for outside organisations. * 6m for the Department of Education of which $5m has been provided for Commonwealth scholarship schemes to cover increases in university fees and the extension of the Aboriginal Secondary Grants Scheme to all children of Aboriginal descent attending secondary schools and classes from the beginning of 1973; $2.5m for education services in the Australian Capital Territory and $700,000 for educational ser vices in the Northern Territory; $3m for the Department of External Territories to cover special assistance to facilitate the transfer of functions to the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Administration, emergency assistance to alleviate food shortages in the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> highlands and salary increases for overseas officers of the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Public Service; $5. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730530_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-55-1)

* A consequential and sensible amount of money is appropriated to cover food aid in the recent difficulties in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730531_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-37-0)

* The scheme for servicemen is based on and is compatible with the superannuation scheme for the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Public Service and police force that came into operation on 1 January, 1972, which will also be the commencing date for the servicemen's scheme. * There are 2 Bills which have 3 broad purposes which may be stated as follows: The first is to transfer responsibility for the Public Service and for the auditing of the accounts of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> to the local executive authority; the second is to implement the recommendations of a report on the future of overseas officers who are in the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Public Service; and the third is to make minor amendments to the description of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> in conformity with the terms of the border agreement entered into between Australia and Indonesia signed in February 1973. * <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730926_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-59-2)

[[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730926_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-59-2)

* It would be most unusual for one sovereign government to guarantee the external borrowings of another sovereign government but this matter will be considered when the detailed arrangements for independence are drawn up after <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> becomes self-governing later this year. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730926_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-59-2)

* As stated by the honourable senator, the Australian Government will continue in the post independence period to honour the guarantees we will have provided for borrowings entered into by the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Government before that time.
