* At the present time borrowings by the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Government which have been guaranteed by the Australian Government amount to more than $300m, including principal and interest. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730926_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-59-2)

* Its purpose is to bring about formal self-government in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> by amending the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Act and by providing the means by which other Australian legislation may be discontinued in its application to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-69-0)

* This legislation marks a significant step towards nationhood for <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-69-0)

* In addition there are 2 Bills which amend specific Australian Acts in their application to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-69-0)

* These amendments result from agreements reached between Australia and <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> for the transfer of the function of the Bureau of Meteorology to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> and the exclusion of that country from the operation of the Wireless Telegraphy Act. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-69-0)

* The amendments proposed to the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Act are certainly historic, but the changes brought about are more symbolic than substantive. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-69-0)

* In practice <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> is virtually self-governing now. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-69-0)

* <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Ministers are at present exercising full responsibilities for most of the functions of internal selfgovernment. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-69-0)

* Each action taken by the Australian Government in moving to self-government in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> has been a deliberate one in a continuing process of transferring responsibility to where it rightly belongs- with the elected representatives of the people of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-69-0)

* Australia has involved the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Government progressively in the full spectrum of government activities- not just in those areas over which final authority has passed. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-69-0)

* Turning first to the Bill to amend the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Act, the amendments contained in this Bill are designed to bring about a formal state of self-government in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> and for the most part will be brought into effect on the agreed date for self-government. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-69-0)

* The previous Australian Government accepted the wishes of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> that the date for self-government be 1 December or as soon as possible thereafter. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-69-0)

* The first is that the legislation we are considering concerns the structure of government in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>, another country, which has a character and an identity of its own. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-69-0)

* Secondly, the amending Bill in the main merely enacts in formal legislative form the de facto situation which has already come about with constitutional development in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-69-0)

* This situation has come about, of course, by agreement with the previous Government as well as this one that there should be a progressive transfer of power from Australia to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Ministers. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-69-0)

* The Bill provides that the Administration will be known as the Government of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-69-0)

* Clause 5 also provides that the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Government is a corporate entity which is able to sue and be sued, and make contracts and agreements by that name. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-69-0)

* The title of the Administrator of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> will be changed to that of the High Commissioner. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-69-0)

* The Bill provides in Clause 8 that subject to the Act the Government shall be administered by the High Commissioner of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-69-0)

* During the self-governing period, the High Commissioner will have 2 functions- those of embryo 'Head of State' for <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> and those of the Australian Representative. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-69-0)

* This accords with the normal constitutional position of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> as a selfgoverning territory of Australia. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-69-0)

* This broadening of its authority reflects current practice agreed by the previous government and this government that when independence comes there will be no area of government in which <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> will be unfamiliar or lack experience. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-69-0)

* Clause 1 1 reflects changes requested by <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> in the composition of the Executive. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-69-0)

* By agreement with <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>, defence and foreign relations will remain reserved to Australia until independence. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-69-0)

* However, again in accordance with agreements reached with <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>, provision has been made for the proclamation at self-government of other functions which it may be necessary to reserve pending completion of any legislative and administrative steps both in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> and Australia. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-69-0)

* Such functions will be proclaimed only after agreement with <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> and as soon as the administrative and legislative details have been completed these functions will be transferred to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-69-0)

* The High Commissioner's role in the reserved areas will be similar to the Administrator's present role in the government of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-69-0)

* As such he will be responsible within <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> for these functions on behalf of Australia and will be subject to the directions of the Australian Government. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-69-0)

* Nevertheless, in accordance with the policies of the previous government and this Government, <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Ministers will be closely and fully involved in the reserved functions. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-69-0)

* The creation of this portfolio and the appointment to it of a <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Minister will ensure that <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> will have first hand involvement and experience in these key reserved areas, well before independence. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-69-0)

* In the light of these changes and in response to a request by the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Government, the Bill by clause 23 amends the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Act to make provision for the laws of the House of Assembly to be called Acts' rather than 'Ordinances' if the House decides to adopt this nomenclature. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-69-0)

* The <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Government has requested that the qualifications of persons who may be appointed as judges of the Supreme Court be extended. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-69-0)

* Amendments under clause 28 will allow lawyers with at least 5 years standing, and judges of courts of unlimited jurisdiction within any legal system similar to that of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> to be apointed Clause 26 provides forjudges to be appointed on contract for a fixed term. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-69-0)

* Such provisions will allow <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> to call on overseas expertise for as long as it takes its own legal profession to provide a sufficient number of judges. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-69-0)

* At present all loans raised by the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Government are guaranteed by Australia by virtue of the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Act. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-69-0)

* I now turn to the second Bill we are consideringthe <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> (Application of Laws) Bill. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-69-0)

* Honourable senators will be aware that there are a number of Acts of the Australian Parliament which have application in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-69-0)

* Some of these Acts apply because the Australian Parliament has expressly extended them to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-69-0)

* Other Acts have application insofar as some sections of them apply to people, things or situations in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-69-0)

* All these Acts form part of the internal law of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-69-0)

* During self-government <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> should be entitled to have the final say on what laws apply within its boundaries, except of course laws in the reserved areas. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-69-0)

* Thus the application of those Australian Acts which would be inconsistent with the status of a self-governing <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> should, so far as practicable, be discontinued. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-69-0)

* The only practicable solution is to permit the making of regulations effectively to cease the application to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> of Australian Acts. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-69-0)

* It is proposed by this Bill that the GovernorGeneral be empowered to make regulations ceasing the operation of Australian Acts in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-69-0)

* The Acts to be dealt with are only those which form part of the internal law of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-69-0)

* To avoid the situation whereby the cessation of an Australian Act would leave a vacuum in the law of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>, it is proposed that the application of an Australian Act, particularly for which there is no <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> counterpart, will in general not be discontinued until and unless that cessation has been approved by the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Government. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-69-0)

* When any Act ceases to apply to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> by regulation, the Act will still apply to Australia. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-69-0)

* It may be that some aspects of that Act, as part of Australian law, but no longer as part of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> law, will require amendment to protect the rights under Australian law of persons, matters or things connected with <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>, or to make provision for the occurrence of matters in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> affecting Australia but not <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-69-0)

* 
 Mr President, I now turn to the 2 other Bills which affect <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>- the Wireless Telegraphy Bill and the Meteorology Bill. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-69-0)

* Briefly both Bills have been drafted to allow for the exclusion of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> from the provisions of the respective Acts by notice in the Gazette. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-69-0)

* <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> and Australia have agreed that both Acts should be discontinued in their application to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> at a mutually agreed time. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-69-0)

* The reasons for this are the enactment by <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> of a radiocommunications ordinance dealing with matters covered by the Wireless Telegraphy Act and the transfer to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> of meteorological functions formerly carried out by the Australian Bureau of Meteorology. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-69-0)

* The amendment to the Meteorology Act provides for the Bureau to continue co-operation with the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> meteorological services. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-69-0)

* 
 Mr President, the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Bill and the other Bills I have detailed form the first of the 2 stages which will bring formal self-government to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-69-0)

* The second stage which will culminate in May or June next year will be the consideration and adoption by the House of Assembly of a Constitution prepared by the Constitutional Planning Committee and the subsequent amendment by this Parliament of the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Act to make the Act consistent with that Constitution. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-69-0)

* These Bills, the adoption of the Constitution, subsequent amendment of the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Act next year, and the final step of independence, are all integral stages in the continuous development of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> from dependency to nationhood. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-69-0)

* The June 1 973 meeting of the United Nations Trusteeship Council endorsed the views of the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> and Australian Governments on the role of the House of Assembly in important constitutional decisions. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-69-0)

* The Council noted the agreement between the Governments of Australia and <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> that resolutions in the House of Assembly on important constitutional issues will be by a recorded vote and by a substantial majority representative of the nation as a whole. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-69-0)

* On the timing of independence, the Council noted Australia's view that there are 2 elements involved in the determination of the question of independence: The view of Australia, and the views of the people of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> as expressed through their elected representatives in the House of Assembly. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-69-0)

* The Council noted that Australia expects independence to come by 1975, and that it should be achieved in the closest consultation with the Government and the House of Assembly of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-69-0)

* I remind honourable senators that the United Nations General Assembly in 1972 asked Australia to fix a timetable for independence in consultation with <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-69-0)

* 
 Mr President, the Bills now before the Senate detail the legislative steps that Australia has to take to enable <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> to be formally self-governing before the end of this year. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-69-0)

* These measures are in accordance with requests by the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Government and the House of Assembly, and have been accepted by the previous Australian Government. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-69-0)

* The amendment of the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Act will formalise the self-governing status of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-69-0)

* This Bill seeks the approval of Parliament to the provision of contractual guarantees by the Australian Government for overseas borrowings by the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Government in foreign currencies not exceeding the equivalent of $A24 million in 1973-74. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-70-0)

* The proceeds of the loans will be used by the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Government to finance public works and services. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-70-0)

* Legislation to authorise the borrowings has already been passed by the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> House of Assembly. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-70-0)

* Last financial year the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Government made its first overseas borrowing on the international capital market. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-70-0)

* The Parliament has also on a number of previous occasions approved similar contractual guarantees by the Australian Government in respect of loans to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> from the International Bank for Reconstruction and Development and the Asian Development Bank. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-70-0)

* All borrowings by the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Government, of course, carry a statutory guarantee by the Australian Government by virtue of section 75A of the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Act. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-70-0)

* Several loan possibilities on overseas markets are currently being investigated by the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Government. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-70-0)

* The form of guarantee that is customarily required in international capital markets is similar to those that have been given to the International Bank for Reconstruction and Development and to the Asian Development Bank in respect of borrowings by <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> from those institutions. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-70-0)

* The Bill is purposely couched in general terms in respect of the currencies and the precise forms of the proposed borrowings so as not to restrict the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Government's choice as to the particular overseas market or markets in which it finally decides to arrange the loans. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-70-0)

* In present circumstances, it is expected that the overall cost of the borrowings by the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Government will be somewhat less than the cost of borrowings for comparable periods form institutional sources in Australia. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-70-0)

* The provision of contractual guarantees by the Australian Government will materially assist <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> in negotiating favourable terms for the borrowings as well as enhancing its status as a borrower on overseas capital markets after it becomes independent. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730927_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-70-0)

* This Banking Bill is one of four Australian bills required to transfer the responsibility for the control and supervision of banking in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> to the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Government and its authorities and to pave the way for the establishment of a separate <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> banking system and central bank. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731017_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-47-0)

* At present the Australian Government's legislation, namely, the Reserve Bank Act, the Banking Act and the Commonwealth Banks Act, extends to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> and, accordingly, the responsibility for control and supervision of banking in that country rests with the Australian Government and, in particular, with the Reserve Bank of Australia. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731017_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-47-0)

* The effect of these Bills will be to withdraw the application of this Australian legislation to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> at a date to be agreed with the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Government and to facilitate the transfer of responsibilities. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731017_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-47-0)

* It will also open the way for the development of a banking and financial system appropriate to the particular needs and circumstances of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> and will ensure control by Papua New Guineans in the planning of future developments in these areas. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731017_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-47-0)

* The development of a separate banking system for <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> was the subject of a detailed examination by a committee of Australian and <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> government officials established by the previous Australian Government. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731017_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-47-0)

* The report of that committee, which was tabled in the Australian Parliament on 29 August 1973, was accepted in principle by the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Government as a suitable basis for action to establish a separate banking system in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731017_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-47-0)

* The principles on which the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> banking system is to be established were set out in a joint Press statement which was issued by the Treasurer  (Mr Crean),  the Minister for External Territories  (Mr Morrison)  and the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Minister for Finance in April 1973. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731017_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-47-0)

* Those principles include: That responsibility for control of banks and financial institutions operating in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> be vested in the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> authorities as soon as practicable; that a central bank be established in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> on the basis of the Port Moresby office of the Reserve Bank of Australia and be endowed with a full range of powers to act as a central monetary authority for a separate banking system, even though some of these powers could not be used in the immediate future; that a national banking institution be established in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> through the setting up of a new <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Government Commercial Bank; and that except where certain accounts give rise to special contractual or financial problems the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> business of the Commonwealth Banking Corporation be transferred to the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Government Commercial Bank. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731017_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-47-0)

* These principles are embodied in two ordinances relating to banking which have recently been passed by the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> House of Assembly. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731017_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-47-0)

* The first of these ordinances is the Central Banking Ordinance which authorises the establishment of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>'s own central bank to be called the Bank of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731017_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-47-0)

* The bank will take over the role at present carried out in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> by the Reserve Bank of Australia. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731017_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-47-0)

* The Australian Government included in its grant to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> this financial year financial assistance to help in the establishment of this new central bank. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731017_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-47-0)

* The <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Government has indicated its intentions, if possible, to bring these two ordinances into force on 1 November 1973. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731017_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-47-0)

* Since the Australian banking legislation extends at present to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>, the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Government can bring these ordinances into operation only when the application of the Australian banking legislation to that country is withdrawn. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731017_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-47-0)

* <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>, and the other associated Bills which I am introducing concurrently to facilitate the establishment of a separate banking system in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731017_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-47-0)

* This Bill provides for the withdrawal of the application of the Reserve Bank Act to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731017_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-49-0)

* As I indicated in introducing the Banking Bill, this Bill is to facilitate the establishment of a separate banking system in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> subject to local control and with its own central bank. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731017_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-49-0)

* This Bill allows for the transfer of certain assets and liabilities from the Reserve Bank of Australia to the Bank of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>, the country's proposed new central bank. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731017_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-50-0)

* It also provides for the transfer of certain assets and liabilities from the Commonwealth Banking Corporation to the proposed new <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Government-owned commercial bank. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731017_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-50-0)

* The provision relating to the Reserve Bank comes in force from the date that the Reserve Bank Act ceases to apply to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731017_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-50-0)

* The provision relating to the Commonwealth Banking Corporation will come into force on the date the Commonwealth Banks Act ceases to apply to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731017_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-50-0)

* The Bill provides for certain business of the Commonwealth Trading Bank and the Commonwealth Savings Bank in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> to be transferred to the proposed new <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Government commercial bank with any necessary settlement to be effected on terms agreed between the two governments. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731017_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-50-0)

* Certain accounts of the Commonwealth Trading Bank giving rise to special contractual or financial problems will not be transferred to the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Bank and this business will be conducted at a special branch of the Commonwealth Trading Bank which will be opened for that purpose and which will be excluded from the transfer. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731017_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-50-0)

* 2) 1973, Reserve Bank Bill 1973, <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> (Transfer of Banking Business) Bill 1973, <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Bill (No. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* 2) 1973, <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> (Application of Laws) Bill 1973, Wireless Telegraphy Bill 1973, Meterology Bill 1973 and <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Loans Guarantee Bill 1973. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* It would be discourteous of the Opposition just to agree to this legislation without any comment because new conditions will result from the independence and self government of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> which we all have watched with interest and have been involved in. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* The Banking Bill is a Bill to amend the Banking Act 1959-1967 and is one of the 4 Bills that are required to transfer the responsibility for the control and supervision of banking in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> to the Government of that country and its authorities. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* This legislation also will pave the way for the setting up of a separate <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> banking system and a central bank in that country. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* At present all of these activities take place under the Australian Government's legislation- the Reserve Bank Act, the Banking Act and the Commonwealth Bank Act- as they extend to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* This move will open up the way for the development of a financial and banking system appropriate to the needs of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* They are that the responsibility for the control of banks and financial institutions operating in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> will take place as soon as practicable and that a central bank be established that will have a full range of power to act as a central monetary authority for a separate banking system. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* But the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> banking system certainly in due course will become the central monetary authority in the independent country of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* Some of these powers may not need to be used in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> immediately but they will be necessary in due course. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* The other operation is that where certain accounts give rise to special contractual or financial problems the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> business of the Commonwealth Banking Corporation will be transferred to the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Government Commercial Bank under certain appropriate arrangements. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* These principles provide a continuity of finance and of operation not only between the governments of the 2 countries but also for those people who are dependent upon that financial support in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> and who may well have entered into some arrangements upon which the continuance of financial support will depend. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* The first of the ordinances that embodies in effect these particular banking activities is the Central Banking Ordinance which authorises the establishment of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> 's own central bank to be called the Bank of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* The Government of Australia has made financial assistance provisions to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> in this financial year to provide for the establishment of that new central bank. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* The <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Government wishes to have these 2 ordinances, if possible, in force on 1 November 1973. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* We cannot in effect let <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> have separate operation until we pass the legislation here. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* This is the third of the Australian Acts relating to banking which extend to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* The Act is being amended to provide that, at a date to be determined, <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> will be excluded from the operation of the Australian Act. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* Once again, it follows the general line of policy which was developed with the Government of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> by the previous Government and to which, as I have observed, we take no objection. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* The greater part of the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> business of the Commonwealth Banking Corporation is to be transferred to a <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Government commercial bank. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* In the paper entitled Australia's External Aid 1973-74', which was presented with the Budget Speech, it will be noted that a payment of $ 15m is to be made to the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Government in 1973-74 to facilitate the establishment of this proposed Government commercial bank; in effect, this payment will help to fund the bank. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* Because of the creation of the new Reserve Bank in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>, the situation concerning the Australian Reserve Bank needs to be altered so that the Australian Reserve Bank no longer operates, in an Australian sense, in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* To me, the financing of cooperative activities- either individual cooperatives or associations of co-operatives- is a very important matter in an emerging country such as <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> where a strong agrarian, fishery type, small trader activity is building up. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* The financing of a great range of small traders through co-operatives is an area that has some hazards for bankers, and I think that the people of this emerging country of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> are entitled to have the expertise of Australian bankers in this field carried on with them and not detached from them too early. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* The next Bill is the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> (Transfer of Banking Business) Bill, which is order of the day No. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* This Bill allows for the transfer of assets and liabilities in certain areas from the Reserve Bank of Australia to the Bank of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>, which is that country's new central bank. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* It also provides for the transfer of certain assets and liabilities from the Commonwealth Banking Corporation to the proposed new <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Government-owned commercial bank. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* The provision comes into force on the date on which the Reserve Bank Act ceases to apply to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* No estimate is given of the amount of money involved on the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Bank's assumption of assets and liabilities and on the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Government-owned commercial bank's assumption of assets and liabilities. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* But certain accounts of the Commonwealth Trading Bank giving rise to special contractual or financial problems will not be transferred to the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Bank, and this business will be conducted at a special branch of the Commonwealth Trading Bank which will be opened for that purpose and which will be excluded from the transfer. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* The Commonwealth Trading Bank will be operating in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> as a banker within its own right. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* I imagine that it will be the first such bank to operate in the style of a foreign bank in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> as an independent country. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* What restrictions will be placed on the Commonwealth Trading Bank in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>? [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* To what extent will it be doing business in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>? [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* Is the bank 's presence in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> limited in time or limited in the amount of money available to it? [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* The continued presence of the Commonwealth Trading Bank in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> is the first stage of Australia, as a nation, engaging in foreign banking. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* Having got to that point, I pass from the banking situation to deal with the Bills which provide for the internal self government of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* I refer to the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Bill, the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> (Application of Laws) Bill, the Wireless Telegraphy Bill and the Meteorology Bill. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* We do not want to hold up the Senate, but I think that those of us who are interested in this matter at least have a responsibility to pay a great tribute to past governments of this country and to past officers of the services of this country, both in the civil sense and in the armed sense, who have contributed so much towards the development of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> in such a peaceful and progressive style. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* I am sure it is not perfect, but set against other examples of administration of countries by overseas powers in what might be called a colonial style- I never cared for it but, never mind, we had a kind of guardianship situation in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>- I believe that the Australian people performed the function well, they discharged it with dignity, they dug fairly deeply into their own pockets to fund the development of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>, and I think that it stands to our credit both with the people of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> and with ourselves, and it certainly stands to our credit with the United Nations and those observers who have been to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> from time to time to witness the progress of that country. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* What we have here is a formal Bill to bring about the formal process of self-government in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* They transfer the functions of the Bureau of Meteorology and they exclude <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> from the operation of the Wireless Telegraphy Act. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* It is perfectly true, as the second reading speech states, that <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> is virtually self-governing now. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* But no Australian would want other than that <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> should progress to independence as fast as is desirable and sensible. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* Because of independence there is a consquential change in the title of the Administrator of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* when independence comes there will be no area of government in which <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> will be unfamiliar or lack experience. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* Clause 1 1 reflects the changes in the Executive as wished by the Government of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* But agreement has been reached with <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> that, on the proclamation of self-government, functions will be taken up which will bring these things under a situation of knowledge and control. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* At the moment in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> there is a portfolio of Defence and Foreign Relations. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* I have some interest in the matter of the loans raised by the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Government because they are guaranteed by Australia by virtue of the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Act. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* 1  think that that is a tribute to the willingness of Australia to underwrite the future of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* A number of Acts of the Australian Parliament have application in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* They are drafted to allow for the exclusion of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> from the provisions of the respective Acts by notice in the Gazette. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* The reasons for this are the enactment by <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> of a radio communications ordinance dealing with matters of wireless telegraphy and the transfer to that country of the meteorological functions formerly carried out by the Australian Bureau of Meteorology. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* These Bills bring about the first of 2 stages towards the formation of selfgovernment for <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>, as mentioned before. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* The final step of independence is the integral stage in the continuous development of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> from dependency to nationhood. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* The June 1973 meeting of the United Nations Trusteeship Council endorsed the views of the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> and Australian Governments on the role of the House of Assembly in important constitutional decisions. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* As mentioned in the second reading speech 2 elements are involved, the view of Australia and the view of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* The <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Loans Guarantee Bill is not a very difficult one. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* It is a Bill to provide for the giving of guarantees by Australia with respect to loans to be raised overseas by <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* It seeks the approval- it is the last Bill of Parliament- to the provision of contractual guarantees by the Australian Government for overseas borrowings by the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Government in foreign currencies not exceeding the equivalent of $24m in 1973-74. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* The Government will have a certain amount tied up which it has guaranteed, and on any future occasion should the Government of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> want to be an overseas borrower in its right and seek the guarantee of the Australian Government, I would expect that a similar Bill would come forward into the Australian Parliament by which the Government would seek the approval of the members of the House of Representatives and of the Senate to give that guarantee. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* In effect, the Government is pledging Australia's credit to a new and independent State, and it is a mark of the Australian people's confidence and willingness to stay in the game of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> that they will give such guarantees. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* It is a further mark in my mind to the credit of the Australian people in all their relations with the emerging independent nation of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* I think that the parliamentary draftsmen who in this somewhat unusual situation have, by their drafting, put into legislative form the ideas and sentiments of the Australian nation and the ideas and sentiments of the new nation of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>, also are deserving of our compliments and appreciation. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* It is important that we should advert at this stage to the fact that a nation like <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> emerging on to the modern world stage cannot do so without continued assistance. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* In the areas which are canvassed in these Bills it becomes apparent that the continued interest and identification of Australia with <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> is of very great importance and will be essential to the proper development and expansion of this new nation and to the emergence of this new country into its proper position in world affairs. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* It is, of course, very much more than that because <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> will have inherited the system of law which we follow, to which we are dedicated and of which we are so extremely proud. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* Therefore the immediate application of our laws within the indigenous and separate <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> context will be of very great importance. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* Therefore we could expect that, allowing for changes that inevitably will take place in any system of law in a different country, substantially the system of the English common law will persist there as it has persisted in the United States, and that the guidance, legal knowledge and expertise of Australia will continue to be available to that country, whether in a general sense or through particular practitioners who will move from our jurisdiction to take their places in judicial and professional positions in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* 1 should be concerned if I thought that on the economic front <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> was merely to be allowed to run adrift, because that could pose tremendous problems not only for that country but also for us. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* Therefore the creation of a central banking system and monetary control disciplines is essential for the economic viability of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* The expertise of the banking institutions of Australia- certainly the public banking institutions and no doubt the private institutions- has been made available and will continue to be made available to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* 1 have not had the opportunity of reading the statement that was made and tabled in August by the Minister as to the consultation between the Commonwealth Bank and the banking authorities in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> on the emergence of the new banking structure, and I should be obliged if the Minister would be kind enough in his reply to indicate the extent to which there will be continuing consultation between the Australian banking institutions- the banking system- and the new banking system of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> so that the most modern banking techniques will continue to be made available. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* If by any chance, due to a lack of knowledge, a lack of ability, a lack of experience, the emerging economy of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> should find itself in a position of economic collapse that would be a tragedy for that nation. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* Therefore, quite apart from our solicitude for <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>, and particularly at this point of time, we have a certain national vested interest that <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>, as it emerges, should be a nation in the full sense of the term economically strong and founded on a proper application of the necessary modern techniques in every area of life to enable it to operate and function efficiently in the interests of its people and to take its place in world affairs, and more particularly to take its place in this area of the world where both it and we have such a common and enduring interest. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* Australia, of course, is one of the most highly developed countries, technically, in the world in all areas of life and perhaps it is therefore fortunate for <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> that this body of knowledge will continue to be made available. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* I have little doubt that it will continue to be made available generously and at all times and continually and that it will be a repository of wisdom, experience and knowledge on which <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> will draw. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* For those reasons I think that at this stage the Senate should register its warm appreciation of the fact that the emergence of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> is moving into the condition where very practical steps are being taken, where the actual organs of government are being created and where with a nice display of prudence and gradualism the institutions are being created. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* I know that there has been criticism in international bodies and throughout the world as to the Australian performance in relation to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* Coincident with that we helped to develop <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> to the point it is at today. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* But I think that it is a matter for tremendous pride that in that time, with those setbacks, we created a nation of our own, one of the wealthiest nations of its size in the world and in the process helped to establish the nation of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> to which independence is now coming with the aid and support that we have been able to give it. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* But they centre around one major Bill, namely, the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Bill (No. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* 2) 1973 to provide for the internal selfgovernment of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* My purpose in speaking in this debate this evening is to make a few general comments concerning the transfer to self-government of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> on 1 December this year. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* I do so primarily because I had the privilege of being the only senator who was a member of a delegation from the Australian Parliament to visit <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> in June of this year. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* Although it is a fact that many honourable senators have visited <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> from time  to  time and many members of the House of Representatives have done so, this delegation of which I was a member was the first official delegation of the Australian Parliament to visit <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* That is the date which I and my fellow members of the delegation found that the people in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> were particularly concentrating upon and, of course, about which they were particularly concerned. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* Dealing with the main Bill before us, the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Bill, the one to effect internal self-government on 1 December, I note that it provides very broadly and we have been all led to understand that after 1 December there will be full internal self-government. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* Apart from that, one would assume that all other powers will be within the competence of the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> House of Assembly and the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Government under its Chief Minister. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* I notice that in the debate on this Bill in another place  Mr Andrew  Peacock, the former Minister for External Territories under the previous Government, raised the question of whether internal self-government meant that the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Government would be entirely responsible for internal security. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* I would have imagined that if <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> had internal self-government, then that Government would be the one entirely responsible for internal security. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* But I raise this problem also because I notice in the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Bill (No. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* I wonder what will be the relationship between the GovernorGeneral and the Government of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> in relation to the recommendation for such appointments. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* As I said, I would assume that certainly the recommendations would come from the Government of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* Senator Byrne  seemed to feel that <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> would maintain a common law system and that the law, as we know it here, will pertain substantially in future in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* From the experience which I gained on my visits to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> and from the discussions which I have had from time to time with people who have lived there, it seems to me that there has been a very real criticism in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> of the administration of our legal system and of the way in which the Supreme Court operates in our legal system. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* It seems to be fairly broadly accepted that the application of the common law and its technical rules has not been particularly successful in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* I believe that the system needs to be watched carefully because the establishment of a village court system, which would apply, as  Senator Byrne  said, local customs in the solution of many problems, may lead to a great fragmentation of the legal system rather than to the provision of a national law which should be the ideal of a new and emerging nation such as <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* I am not saying that that is proposed in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* I rose because I was a member of a quite recent parliamentary delegation to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* We had a remarkable opportunity to meet diverse elements of the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> community. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* I think that local councils have been among the great achievements of the Australian administration of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* It was from our discussions with them that we, I think, were able to appreciate some of the major concerns which face the inhabitants of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> as they move towards self government. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* The people of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> are quite satisfied and quite content with the notion of" self government. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* I am not saying that it is not our obligation to endeavour to hasten along the processes of independence, but I think it is my duty to express in the national Parliament, having had this opportunity to visit <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>, the concern that so many people there feel about this matter. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* Nevertheless I think it is our responsibility to keep emphasising this matter to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> at every opportunity we have because undoubtedly there was this feeling that once we handed over to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> we, as a nation, would tend to reduce financial assistance or eliminate it entirely. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* This has particular personification in the localisation of positions in the various elements of the public service in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> and will be related to the time for which Australians- expatriates as they are known- continue to remain and work in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* They are very conscious of the importance of the participation of Australians and other expatriates, now and for many years to come, in providing expert services in so many fields of government in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* Among them are men and women who went there at an early age and who have devoted their lives to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* Guinea but also in Australia, among those who take an interest in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> as to what is the Australian Government's policy in relation to independence. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* So in this respect there is great confusion, not only in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> but also in Australia. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* We as a Party have taken the view that independence should not be thrust upon <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>, that there should be a request to us by a representative body of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> which says: 'We are now ready for independence. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* Not only is there concern about independence but also a number of local movements, even secessionist movements, are starting to arise in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* These matters have to be resolved primarily, of course, by the Papua New Guineans themselves, and the decisions have to be made by the only representative body of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>, namely, the House of Assembly. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* Members of the Labor Party who have this conscience problem about this matter want to unburden <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> as quickly as possible. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* We cannot just throw independence at <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> before these matters are resolved in some way or other because if we do we will only be leaving the country with a Government which will then be racked by internal civil war. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* The <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Select Committee on Constitutional Development which is already sitting and working in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> is, I believe, likely to come forward with some proposals in this regard. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* I believe that there will have to be many more of this sort of development before <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> is fully fit for independence. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* Because after 1 December we as a national parliament will still have responsibility for <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>'s foreign affairs and defence and, I think, for a general oversight of the affairs of that nation, we ourselves will have to shoulder some considerable responsibility in determining this vital question of independence. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* I would like to add my dissident voice to the rush towards independence in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* When I first took an interest in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> I was of the opinion that it needed its independence, but the more I studied the country and the more I went up there the more I realised that it was not yet time for independence. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* It is all very well to say that we have to give independence to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> as fast as possible, but when one looks around the country one can see that the people are not ready for it and many do not want it. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* They want us to rush into giving independence to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> because they will be the heads of government in the country. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* I cannot understand why we have to impose our system of democracy on <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* -Oh, yes, but it is not so good that the people of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> have to conform to our way of doing things and must have a parliament which is totally different in type from that which they are used to. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* We are insisting on imposing our morality on the people of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* We are insisting on <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> adopting our education system, and probably our education system is better. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* For years we have been trying to impose our laws on the people of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>, but are our laws any better than theirs? [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* -The army will not be dissolved by then because it will be the only means of maintaining law and order in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>, and that will be the most powerful arm in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* Certainly they may have made a profit from living there, but without them <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> would not be where is is today. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

[[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* What the Japanese could not achieve during the war they will certainly achieve economically in the next few years if we do not be firm in our relations with <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* Giving <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> independence does not seem to me to be the answer, but it seems the 'in' thing nowadays is that every nation must have its independence whether or not it is ready, and it seems that we have to assist <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> towards independence. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* Because one of the Administrators wanted a job for himself there he decided that a university was needed, so we rushed ahead and founded that university, and the standard was lowered because no one in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> could reach matriculation level. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* That is all right if that is the way that the people of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> want it, but I do not think that they really wanted a university. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* I think we have failed the people of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> in education and in medicine, and I think we are going to fail them altogether when we hand over independence to them.
