* In the report of the Committee on Banking in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> in November last year it is proposed that legislation for this purpose be enacted in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>; and that the Reserve Bank of Australia be asked to provide appropriate technical assistance for the new central bank for as long as may be necessary in order to maintain efficient operations following transfer. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* In regard to the Commonwealth Banking Corporation it is proposed that the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> business of the Corporation be transferred as soon as practicable to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Government ownership; that the Corporation should not compete for banking business with the Government Commercial Bank following the transfer as such competition at that time would prejudice the success of the transfer; that the Corporation be asked to provide appropriate managerial and technical assistance to the Government's Commercial Bank for as long as may be necessary to maintain efficient operations following the transfer; that the extent to which, consistent with the above information, the Corporation should be permitted to continue to engage in banking business in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>, particularly in cases where there may be special contractual or financial problems involved in the transfer of accounts, should be a matter for further detailed consideration by the appropriate authorities. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* I think that the short answer is that the Commonwealth Bank will have an influence on and give guidance to the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> bank for as long as is necessary. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731023_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-57-0)

* I interpolate here that the proposal in a subsequent Bill to levy a withholding tax of 15 per cent on dividends paid from Australia to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> will result in there being some Australian tax on dividends paid in furture to respository companies in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. * To correct the situation, the Bill proposes basically that where dividends were, or are, paid after 19 July 1972 by a private company in Australia to another private company in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>, they will not be taken into account in determining whether the paying company has made a distribution of profits sufficient to avoid payment of undistributed profits tax. * This is the basic provision but there are measures to the effect that it is to apply to dividends that are held in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> on behalf of Australian individual shareholders. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740409_senate_28_s59/#subdebate-34-0)

* He was a member of the delegation that attended the first meeting of the Legislative Council of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740710_senate_29_s60/#subdebate-36-0)

* My goodness, they were very articulate when they urged <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> on to a state of nationhood and independence- very much so. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740717_senate_29_s60/#subdebate-45-0)

* Much of this lending has gone to developing countries of interest to Australia in the Asian and Pacific regions, including <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740718_senate_29_s60/#subdebate-57-0)

* I can recall the controversy that arose about a case in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>, I think- not in Australia- which reached the High Court of Australia and in which there had been an interpretation of an interpretation. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740724_senate_29_s60/#subdebate-31-0)

* They are in Asia in particular and in the Pacific region, including <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740724_senate_29_s60/#subdebate-51-0)

* In addition, a substantial amount of IBRD money has been borrowed by <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740724_senate_29_s60/#subdebate-51-0)

* As honourable senators know from previous debate in this chamber, we have guaranteed the indebtedness of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> at the point of its obtaining independence and for some stage unascertained but implicit beyond that point of time. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740724_senate_29_s60/#subdebate-51-0)

* So we for our own part and on behalf of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> have a fairly substantial capital debt that we might think about relieving if we find ourselves not quite so flush. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740724_senate_29_s60/#subdebate-51-0)

* Will Australian servicemen be with the armed forces of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> after that nation achieves independence on 1 December next? [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740730_senate_29_s60/#subdebate-26-0)

* As the Senate knows, over a long period of time we have been allowing <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> to do everything that it can do itself. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740730_senate_29_s60/#subdebate-26-0)

* In his speech at the opening of Parliament, the Governor-General pointed out that we were now treating <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>, to the fullest extent possible, as an independent country. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740730_senate_29_s60/#subdebate-26-0)

* When <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> declares its independence it will be more or less a formal declaration. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740730_senate_29_s60/#subdebate-26-0)

* He may be interested to know that there are several Territories for which the Australian Parliament and people are responsible- the Australian Antarctic Territory, Christmas Island, Cocos Keeling Island, the Coral Sea islands, Heard Island, Macdonald Island, the New Guinea Trust Territory, Norfolk Island, Ashmore and Carrier Islands, and <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740806_senate_29_s60/#subdebate-4-0)

* From Press reports I have learnt that 2 representatives of the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> branch of the Returned Services League are at present in Australia. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740813_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-19-0)

* It has been reported that they have come here to seek benefits for death and injury suffered by indigenous inhabitants of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> who served with the Australian armed forces during the Second World War. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740813_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-19-0)

* However, at no stage has the national office of the League in any way indicated to me that these people from the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> branch are in Australia. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740813_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-19-0)

* The War Cabinet during the Second World War made provision for the payment of compensation to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> servicemen or their dependants in the case of injury or death. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740813_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-19-0)

* Following the war the repatriation benefits generally were extended to indigenous inhabitants of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740813_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-19-0)

* Provision is being made under existing legislation for the continuation of the payment of these repatriation benefits after <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> obtains independence. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740813_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-19-0)

* Can the Minister for Repatriation and Compensation inform the Senate about arrangements for the provision of repatriation benefits for Australian ex-servicemen and their dependants who will continue to reside in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> after independence? [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740814_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-23-0)

* Upon the attainment of independence by <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> there will be no difference in the situation of people who fall into those categories. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740814_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-23-0)

* If nothing were to be done about this matter, upon the attainment of independence by <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> a number of people who are at present living there would lose that benefit because <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> would cease to be a Territory. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740814_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-23-0)

* However, the Government recently considered the matter and decided that any person who received these latter benefits and who was living in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> at the date of independence would be deemed to continue to be a resident of Australia or of one of its Territories and would continue to receive the benefits. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740814_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-23-0)

* However, if somebody was not a resident of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> at the date of independence and subsequently went to live there, he would fall into the same category as persons who have moved out of Australia and its Territories to a foreign country and would not be in receipt of the latter type of benefit. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740814_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-23-0)

* He was a member of the delegation representing the Australian Parliament at die inauguration of the Legislative Council for <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> in November 1951. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740917_senate_29_s61/#debate-2)

* For the information of honourable senators I present the report on the Administration of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> for the year ended 30 June 1973. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740917_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-35-0)

* -These 2 Bills which have been taken together relate to the exercise by the self governing legislature of the Territory of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> of certain powers with respect to offshore mining. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740924_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-58-0)

* The Opposition recognises that the Bills clarify a matter of some doubt in one respect and acknowledge the rights of the Territory of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> at this stage, and certainly when it becomes independent, to exercise full and plenary powers over exploration for mining in its off-shore areas. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740924_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-58-0)

* The present position in relation to the power to make laws with regard to off-shore mining is that the provisions of the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Act have been exercised in the manner in which, prior to self government last December, the power to make laws was transferred from the Australian Government to the legislature of the Territory of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740924_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-58-0)

* Accepting that when the Territory of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> becomes independent it should have all the powers of a sovereign nation with regard to its off-shore areas, it is appropriate that there be no doubt that <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> on independence will have that power. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740924_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-58-0)

* I understand that that is the sole purpose of the amendment to the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Act. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740924_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-58-0)

* The amendment to the Petroleum (Submerged Lands) Act is designed to carry forward logically and, one might suppose, is a matter of realisation of what was contemplated some 7 years ago, that some day the Territory of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> would exercise for itself powers with regard to petroleum exploration and exploitation in its off-shore waters. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740924_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-58-0)

* It will mean that the Petroleum (Submerged Lands) Act passed by this Parliament hereafter will contain no reference to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> and impliedly will divest all Australian authorities of power to make laws with regard to exploration for and exploitation of petroleum in the off-shore waters. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740924_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-58-0)

* In the negotiations which took place prior to that agreement and in the terms of the agreement the Australian Government acted on behalf of the Territory of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740924_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-58-0)

* It is my recollection that the Minister for Foreign Affairs has been the Designated Authority in regard to the Territory of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>, he having succeeded the Minister for External Territories. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740924_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-58-0)

* The territorial division of the submerged lands area between Queensland and the Territory of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> was a fundamental part of the arrangement so that the area over which the Commonwealth Government, representing the Territory of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>, would exercise authority could be differentiated from the area over which the Designated Authority for the State of Queensland would exercise authority. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740924_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-58-0)

* I understand, having had some discussions with  Mr Peacock  who represents the Opposition in this matter in the House of Representatives, that the boundary which was drawn in 1967 has undergone some inevitable changes over the years, so that what is now produced in the legislation which is currently before us is a boundary which includes part of the land mass of the Territory of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740924_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-58-0)

* As I have indicated these 2 Bills are part of the ongoing process, with which the Opposition concurs, for the transference of power to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> so that when it assumes independence it will be a full independence in which the co-operation of the Australian Government at all times has been evident. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740924_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-58-0)

* The Australian Country Party will support the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Bill and the Petroleum (Submerged Lands) Bill. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740924_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-58-0)

* However, the boundary between Queensland and <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> has received a great deal of attention in the past. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740924_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-58-0)

* Honourable senators will appreciate, of course, that I am deputising in the carriage of the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Bill and the Petroleum (Submerged Lands) Bill on behalf of my colleague, the Minister for Foreign Affairs  (Senator Willesee). [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740924_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-58-0)

* I am told that the Bill does not extend to the Queensland adjacent area but that it extends to the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> area and does not affect in any way the economics of the matter. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740924_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-58-0)

* The Bill provides for Australia to accede to the Convention with a declaration that it is to extend to all our external Territories except <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19741002_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-40-0)

* With regard to our development assistance to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>, we endorse the objectives of the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Government's 1973-74 Improvement Plan to achieve a more equitable distribution of the benefits of development, and will keep under continual review the question of how our development assistance can best support this objective. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19741016_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-53-10)

* 8m-A$7.3m- borrowing by the Government of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> from the International Bank for Reconstruction and Development. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19741017_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-47-0)

* The proceeds of the loan will assist in financing the development and expansion of the operations of the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Electricity Commission during the period 1974-79. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19741017_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-47-0)

* This loan follows a loan for US$23.2m-$A15.6m-to the Electricity Commission in 1971 to assist in financing a major hydro-electric project on the Upper Ramu River in the highlands of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19741017_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-47-0)

* The loan documents were signed by authorised representatives of the Australian Government on 12 June following negotiations in Washington which were attended by representatves of the International Bank, Australia, the Government of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> and the Electricity Commission. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19741017_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-47-0)

* The Government of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> will onlend the proceeds of the loan to the Electricity Commission which, under an associated project agreement between the Commission and the Bank, is responsible for the project. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19741017_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-47-0)

* Borrowings by the Government of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> automatically carry an Australian Government guarantee by virtue of the operation of section 75 A of the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Act 1949-1973. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19741017_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-47-0)

* The guarantee agreement for this loan, which is shown as the First Schedule to the Bill, follows the form of the 4 guarantee agreements previously approved by Parliament in connection with a telecommunications loan made by the International Bank to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> in 1968, a highways loan made in 1970, the first hydro-electric project loan in 1971 and a second telecommunications project loan in 1 972. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19741017_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-47-0)

* This Bill seeks the approval of Parliament to the provision of contractual guarantees by the Australian Government for overseas borrowings by the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Government in foreign currencies not exceeding the equivalent of $A20m prior to achievement of independence in 1974-75. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19741017_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-48-0)

* The proceeds of the loans will be used by the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Government to finance public works and services. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19741017_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-48-0)

* In the 1 972-73 financial year the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Government made its first overseas borrowing on the international capital market. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19741017_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-48-0)

* Under the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Loans Guarantee Act 1973 guarantee for loans of 5 billion yen and 50 million Swiss francs have also been given. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19741017_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-48-0)

* Parliament has also, on a number of previous occasions, approved similar contractual guarantees by the Australian Government in respect of loans to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> from the International Bank for Reconstruction and Development and the Asian Development Bank. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19741017_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-48-0)

* Loan possibilities on overseas markets are currently being investigated by the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Government. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19741017_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-48-0)

* The form of guarantee that is customarily required in international capital markets is similar to those that have been given to the International Bank for Reconstruction and Development and to the Asian Development Bank in respect of borrowings by <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> from those institutions. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19741017_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-48-0)

* The Bill is purposely couched in general terms in respect of the currencies and the precise forms of the proposed borrowings so as not to restrict the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Government's choice as to the particular overseas markets in which it finally decides to arrange the loans. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19741017_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-48-0)

* The provision of contractual guarantees by the Australian Government will materially assist <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> in negotiating favourable terms for the borrowings as well as enhancing its status as a borrower on overseas capital markets. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19741017_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-48-0)

* The <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Loans Guarantee Bill is a straightforward measure. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19741017_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-48-0)

* It is mentioned in the second reading speech that <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> engaged in its first overseas borrowing in the year 1972-73. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19741017_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-48-0)

* This is a guarantee arrangement to cover <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> as it passes towards independence. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19741017_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-48-0)

* This Bill gives <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> a more favourable opportunity in the international money market. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19741017_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-48-0)

* It allows <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> to achieve a more effective interest rate. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19741017_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-48-0)

* It is couched in general terms, as is expressed in the second reading speech, so that the currencies in which <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> may wish to negotiate are open for it to judge. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19741017_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-48-0)

* This Bill allows us to give <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> a guarantee by underwriting loans. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19741017_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-48-0)

* Because of the inadequacy of past arrangements, also recognised by the Joint Parliamentary Foreign Affairs Committee's 1972 inquiry into Australia's foreign aid, the Prime Minister, in March last year, commissioned a task force 'to examine all the options for a unified aid administration to administer all aid including multilateral aid, all bilateral aid and aid to an independent <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>'. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19741022_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-44-0)

* Mr L.  W. Johnson, former Administrator and High Commissioner to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>, was appointed on 8th April this year as its DirectorGeneral. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19741022_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-44-0)

* This is a combined Bill which will authorise changes to the Repatriation Act, the Interim Forces Benefits Act, the Repatriation (Far East Strategic Reserve) Act, the Repatriation (Special Overseas Service) Act, the Native Members of the Forces Benefits Act to be retitled the '<span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> (Members of the Forces Benefits) Act', and the Seamen's War Pensions and Allowances Act. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19741024_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-50-0)

* Retention of eligibility for repatriation benefits which are available only to residents in Australia and its Territories will be proposed in respect of Australian veterans and their dependants who are resident in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> prior to that country gaining independence, and who continue to reside there. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19741024_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-50-0)

* Australians Resident in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> after Independence [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19741024_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-50-0)

* Many of these people have spent many years in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> and have established their means of livelihood there, and it would seem unjust to deprive them of benefits because of changed circumstances beyond their control. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19741024_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-50-0)

* The Government proposes to allow persons resident in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> prior to that country gaining its independence, and who continue to reside there after independence, to be then considered still resident in Australia or its Territories for repatriation purposes. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19741024_senate_29_s61/#subdebate-50-0)

* I think it will be agreed by most members of the Senate that this particular Bill is more extensive than many we have debated because it brings under the principal Act, the Repatriation Act 1920-1973, the following Bills to which it will authorise changes: The Interim Forces Benefits Act, the Repatriation (Far East Strategic Reserve) Act, the Repatriation (Special Overseas Service) Act, the Native Members of the Forces Benefits Act to be retitled the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> (Members of the Forces Benefits) Act, and the Seamen's War Pensions and Allowances Act. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19741029_senate_29_s62/#subdebate-38-0)

* It may interest honourable senators who have not studied the Bill- if there are any- to know that the independence of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> is acknowledged and the effect on ex-servicemen resident in that emerging country is covered by this Bill. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19741029_senate_29_s62/#subdebate-38-0)

* In other words, those who are entitled to repatriation benefits, service pensions and the like who are going to remain living in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> will, under this Bill, be able to draw their Australian entitlements. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19741029_senate_29_s62/#subdebate-38-0)

* Since 1 May 1973, he has been Assistant Secretary in charge of the Pacific Branch which covers both <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> and the South Pacific. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19741029_senate_29_s62/#subdebate-42-1)

* Clearly we have a responsibility to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> and our present level of assistance there must continue for some time. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19741030_senate_29_s62/#subdebate-31-0)

* Although I admit that I was delighted that the Agency has the new responsibility of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> added to the responsibilities of the former aid office, I find it hard to justify this very significant increase in staff. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19741030_senate_29_s62/#subdebate-31-0)

* We must do all we can to help <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> become a mature nation. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19741112_senate_29_s62/#debate-45)

* At certain periods of the year the Fly River, which runs out of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> into the Bay of Papua, brings down enormous quantities of rubbish including big logs. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19741114_senate_29_s62/#subdebate-40-0)

* The five patrol boats transferred to the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Defence Force were built in the late 1960's specifically to undertake tasks in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> waters. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19741114_senate_29_s62/#subdebate-45-8)

* Since these tasks will now be performed by the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Defence Force, the five patrol boats need not be replaced. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19741114_senate_29_s62/#subdebate-45-8)

* In addition, as the scheme now stands, investments in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> are specifically excluded from the scope of the scheme. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19741126_senate_29_s62/#subdebate-57-0)

* Also, in recognition of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>'s expressed desire for increased Australian investment to further its social and economic development plans, it is proposed to extend the scope of the overseas investment insurance scheme to cover new eligible investments in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19741126_senate_29_s62/#subdebate-57-0)

* In addition, IDA has lent a total of US$25.2m to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> to date. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19741126_senate_29_s62/#subdebate-59-0)

* The Bill also proposes some technical amendments concerned with the allowance in tax assessments of our residents of a credit for <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> tax on income derived there. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19741126_senate_29_s62/#subdebate-69-0)

* The amendments, which were foreshadowed in an announcement made by the Treasurer last year, are consequential upon the introduction of a dividend withholding tax by <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> in August 1 972 and will ensure that appropriate credit is allowed for that tax. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19741126_senate_29_s62/#subdebate-69-0)

* In particular, the purpose here is to assist <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> with its development and to assist and encourage Australian private investment in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> after that country gets its independence. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19741128_senate_29_s62/#subdebate-60-0)

* Previously <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> was excluded from the provisions of the overseas investment insurance scheme which was administered by the Export Payments Insurance Corporation, but now that <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> is about to become independent- it is in fact self-governing- and because of Australia's great interest in the economic development of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>, we are particularly interested in and welcome the provisions which expand this insurance scheme to cover <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19741128_senate_29_s62/#subdebate-60-0)

* The reason behind this was that there were people from, say, <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> and other places who might want to come here, study for their course and be admitted. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19741203_senate_29_s62/#subdebate-57-0)

* The purpose of this Bill is to amend the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Act 1949-1974 to enable Australia to transfer to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> responsibility for those matters which at present remain reserved to Australia, as soon as their transfer is requested by the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Government. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19741204_senate_29_s62/#subdebate-43-0)

* This is in line with Australia's policy of ensuring that <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> exercises final responsibility in all matters of government before assuming full independence. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19741204_senate_29_s62/#subdebate-43-0)

* Clause 3 of the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Bill (No. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19741204_senate_29_s62/#subdebate-43-0)

* 2) amends section 5 (1a) of the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Act. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19741204_senate_29_s62/#subdebate-43-0)

* The matters so specified are: the Supreme Court of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> and all other courts established by <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> enactment; authority in relation to legal aid; responsibility for instituting prosecutions; House of Assembly and electoral policy matters. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19741204_senate_29_s62/#subdebate-43-0)

* Honourable senators will recall that authority over those matters was reserved to Australia at self-government at the specific request of the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Government. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19741204_senate_29_s62/#subdebate-43-0)

* Clause 3 of the Bill provides for the omission of paragraphs (a) and (b) of sub-section 5 ( 1a) of the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Act. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19741204_senate_29_s62/#subdebate-43-0)

* When <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> requests the transfer of authority over these two matters the repeal of those paragraphs will in effect be proclaimed. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19741204_senate_29_s62/#subdebate-43-0)

* The reservation of the remaining matters can also be brought to an end by proclamation on request by <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19741204_senate_29_s62/#subdebate-43-0)

* <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> has already introduced its defence legislation in the House of Assembly and when this has been enacted Australian defence legislation will need to be amended to enable the completion of the transfer of authority. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19741204_senate_29_s62/#subdebate-43-0)

* The exercise of responsibility by the Government of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> in the areas of defence and foreign relations until formal independence must be subject to Australia's treaty obligations and responsibilities in international law and to the United Nations under the Charter and the Trusteeship Agreement. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19741204_senate_29_s62/#subdebate-43-0)

* However the transfer of final control to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> within this framework will allow <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> to give effect to its own policies and priorities in these matters, policies and priorities which in fact it is already formulating. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19741204_senate_29_s62/#subdebate-43-0)

* As I have said, Australian policy is to enable <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> to exercise authority in all matters of government before the formal step to independence, and these amendments are designed to give effect to this. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19741204_senate_29_s62/#subdebate-43-0)

* Clauses 4 to 9 of the Bill relate to Part VI of the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Act- the judicial system. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19741204_senate_29_s62/#subdebate-43-0)

* Part VI of the Act is amended by the Bill to provide for the functions now assigned to and powers held by the Governor-General under sections 58 to 61 of the Act to be conferred on and exercised by the High Commissioner of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19741204_senate_29_s62/#subdebate-43-0)

* In line with these amendments the Governor-General 's instructions to the High Commissioner will require him to act on the advice of the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Government in exercising his functions under Part VI of the Act. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19741204_senate_29_s62/#subdebate-43-0)

* Sub-section 62a (6) of the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Act at present authorises the Governor-General to disallow rules of court. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19741204_senate_29_s62/#subdebate-43-0)

* The <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Government has requested that when the transfer of authority over judicial matters takes place section 64 of the Act should be repealed. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19741204_senate_29_s62/#subdebate-43-0)

* Section 64 of the Act provides that the Australian High Court has jurisdiction to hear and determine appeals from all judgments, decrees, orders and sentences of a Full Court of the Supreme Court of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19741204_senate_29_s62/#subdebate-43-0)

* Clause 10 of the Bill amends section 73 (2) of the Act to empower the High Commissioner to grant pardon, remission, commutation or respite of sentence to an offender sentenced to death by a court exercising criminal jurisdiction in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19741204_senate_29_s62/#subdebate-43-0)

* The purpose of this Bill is to amend the Judges' Pensions Act 1968-1973 to provide for the payment of pensions to persons who are or have been judges of the Supreme Court of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> (<span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Judges) and to their dependants. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19741204_senate_29_s62/#subdebate-44-0)

* The Bill has been prepared after consultation with the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> judges. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19741204_senate_29_s62/#subdebate-44-0)

* The Supreme Court will continue to exist by virtue of Part VI of the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Act, but appointments of judges made by the Governor-General under section 59 of that Act will cease to have effect on and after 1 December 1974. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19741204_senate_29_s62/#subdebate-44-0)

* At present, pensions are payable to those judges and to former judges and their dependants by virtue of the Judges' Pensions Act- formerly Ordinance- 1969 of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19741204_senate_29_s62/#subdebate-44-0)

* The effect of the Bill will be to bring those of the present Judges who were appointed before 1 December 1973, the date on which <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> achieved selfGovernment, under the Australian Judges' Pensions Act, so that their pension rights are guaranteed by Australian legislation. * Clause 4 provides that a <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> judge appointed before 1 December 1973 who has attained the age of 55 years and who retires after serving as a judge for not less than 10 years will be entitled to a full pension at a rate equal to 60 per centum of the 'appropriate current judicial salary'. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19741204_senate_29_s62/#subdebate-44-0)

* Such a judge who not being otherwise entitled to a full pension, ceases to hold office as a judge because his services are no longer required by the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Government will receive a full pension irrespective of his length of service. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19741204_senate_29_s62/#subdebate-44-0)

* It applies the Bill to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Judges who may have retired or died before the commencement of the clause, so that they or their dependants will receive pensions under the Bill. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19741204_senate_29_s62/#subdebate-44-0)

* It provides for increased tax liabilities for the mining industry, the imposition of taxation on certain forms of fringe benefits, specific allowance of deductions for depreciation on child care facilities, a reduction of the limit on deductions for educational expenses, the deductibility of mortgage interest payments, a reduced level of the special deduction allowable to life assurance companies, a rebate of dependants' allowances for low income families, technical amendments of the principal Act with respect to dividends payable from <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> and the relief for taxpayers in cases of hardship arising out of provisional tax for 1974-75. * Does the Government of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> have the power to unilaterally change the year of an election, or would this require amending an Australian Act of Parliament? [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750408_senate_29_s63/#subdebate-63-6)

* The Chief Minister,  Mr Somare,  spoke against the motion, which is not binding on the Government of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750408_senate_29_s63/#subdebate-63-6)

* That <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> do move to independent nation status as soon as practicable after a constitution has been enacted by this House and that any proposed date for independence is to be endorsed by this House. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750408_senate_29_s63/#subdebate-63-6)

* The current legislation governing the holding of elections in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> is the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Act 1949-1974. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750408_senate_29_s63/#subdebate-63-6)

* This provides for the High Commissioner of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> to direct at any time the holding of a general election but that general elections shall be held at intervals not exceeding four years. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750408_senate_29_s63/#subdebate-63-6)

* After independence, the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Act will not apply and elections will be held in accordance with the provisions of the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Constitution, the terms of which are currently being debated by the House of Assembly. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750408_senate_29_s63/#subdebate-63-6)

* We are seeing instability in Timor and instability threatens in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750409_senate_29_s63/#subdebate-33-0)

* Of this, $70m is for payment to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> to facilitate the purchase from Australia of defence assets associated with the transfer of the responsibility for the defence function to that Government. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750421_senate_29_s63/#subdebate-38-1)

* There is an amount of $152m for defence, $70m of which is to be paid to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> to purchase from Australia the defence assets that are there. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750422_senate_29_s63/#subdebate-47-0)

* The Bill proposes other amendments to the principal Act, the most important of which concern the acceptability of savings held in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750515_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-36-0)

* Unless appropriate amendments are made, changes to the banking system in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> associated with the granting of self-government may prejudice the possible eligibility of some Australians temporarily working and saving in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750515_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-36-0)

* Furthermore, under the terms of the present Act, savings held with any bank in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> would cease to be acceptable for purposes of the Home Savings Grant Scheme on and after the date of independence. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750515_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-36-0)

* To overcome these problems, the Bill proposes amendments that will ensure that savings held with any bank in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> in similar forms to those acceptable in the case of banks in Australia will continue to be acceptable until 31 December 1976, that is, until the last day on which savings held in Australia will be acceptable. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750515_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-36-0)

* Fights between races have taken place in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750515_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-46-0)
