* From that date the ABC will supply its radio programs as they are requested by the National Broadcasting Commission of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750521_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-4-0)

* The <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Broadcasting [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750521_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-4-0)

* The following precautions are taken by the Government to prevent the introduction of rabies into Australia: Dogs and cats may be imported only from certain rabies free countries, namely, New Zealand, the United Kingdom, the Republic of Ireland, <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>, Fiji, Hawaii and Norfolk Island. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750522_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-3-0)

* Clause 25 empowers the Tribunal to sit at any place in Australia or in an external Territory other than <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750527_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-47-0)

* One purpose of this Bill is to amend the Australian income tax law so that when <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> becomes independent it will be treated as a separate country for Australian tax purposes. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750605_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-42-0)

* Our income tax law contains a number of special provisions relating to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750605_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-42-0)

* Some relate to an administrative position that came about in 1959 when a separate income tax was imposed in the Territory of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750605_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-42-0)

* In broad terms, those provisions that provide special treatment for certain categories of income or expenditure related to activities conducted in either Australia or <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>, but not in other countries, will be made inapplicable by the Bill so far as concerns income and expenditure related to activities conducted in an independent <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750605_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-42-0)

* Subject to some exceptions, income derived from a source in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> by Australian residents will be treated in the same way for Australian Tax purposes as income from a source in other places outside Australia. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750605_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-42-0)

* Residents of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> will be taxed like other nonresidents on income from sources in Australia. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750605_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-42-0)

* A tax credit system at present applies in respect of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> income of Australian residents and in the converse case. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750605_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-42-0)

* It is proposed to retain this system in Australia after independence but, as the Treasurer  (Dr J. F. Cairns)  announced recently, the salary or wages of Australians working in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> will be exempted from Australian tax where <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> taxes the income. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750605_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-42-0)

* The rate of withholding tax on dividends paid to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> residents is half the general rate of 30 per cent. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750605_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-42-0)

* We propose however to continue it in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>'s case after independence. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750605_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-42-0)

* The Bill generally requires the changes I have described to be synchronised with <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>'s independence. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750605_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-42-0)

* In this connection I mention that we will be giving sympathetic consideration to a request that the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Government has recently foreshadowed it will make for some extension of these transitional arrangements in relation to mineral exploration expenditure by Australian companies in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750605_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-42-0)

* The Bill also contains some other measures related to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>'s independence. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750605_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-42-0)

* One of these is that, on a basis of reciprocity, people in receipt of pensions from Australia or <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> are to be taxed only in whichever of the 2 countries they reside. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750605_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-42-0)

* Another will confer an exemption from Australian tax on compensation and allowances paid under the employment security scheme now authorised by the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> (Staffing Assistance) Act 1973. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750605_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-42-0)

* These amounts are paid to members of the Australian Staffing Assistance Group and other former expatriate officers of the Public Service of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> on termination of their services there. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750605_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-42-0)

* It seeks to amend the tax law so that after independence <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> will be treated as a separate country for Australian tax purposes. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750612_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-41-0)

* The Bill ends the operation of special provisions applying to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750612_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-41-0)

* Income that is derived from <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> by Australian residents will be treated as income from a source outside Australia. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750612_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-41-0)

* Salary or wages of Australians working in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> under various attachments or contracts to that Government will be exempt from Australian tax where the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Government taxes the income. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750612_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-41-0)

* The rate of withholding tax on dividends paid to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> residents will remain at half the general rate of 30 per cent, despite the fact that there is no comprehensive double tax agreement with <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750612_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-41-0)

* The changes are to be synchronised with the independence of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>, whenever that comes about. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750612_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-41-0)

* People in receipt of pensions from Australia or <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> will be taxed only in the country of residence. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750612_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-41-0)

* Exemptions from Australian tax on compensation and allowances paid under the employment security scheme are only to the extent that the amount is of a kind prescribed by the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> (Staffing Assistance) (Termination of Employment) Regulations. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750612_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-41-0)

* They are the amounts which are paid to expatriate officers of the Public Service of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> at the end of their service there. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750612_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-41-0)

* I found, of course, what I ought to have known, that the benefits were tied up in this major Bill affecting the situation in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750612_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-41-0)

* The answer is that the Soviet Ambassador has issued a statement saying that the question of Soviet financial aid to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> was not specifically raised in the talks that he had in Port Moresby. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750819_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-24-0)

* According to Press reports,  Sir Maori  Kiki has stated that he regarded the Ambassador's remarks at the Press conference about the possibility of some Soviet aid being made available to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> as just an offer and that there were no plans to discuss the matter further. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750819_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-24-0)

* Sir Maori  is also reported as saying that his talks with the Soviet Ambassador came before and had no relationship to the Australian decision on aid to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> this year. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750819_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-24-0)

* The Australian Government would be happy to see more countries grant aid to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> on terms acceptable to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750819_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-24-0)

* I have often said that myself and have tried to encourage other countries to do just that, to help in contributing to the development of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750819_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-24-0)

* It is a sorry but hardly surprising state of affairs to find  Mr Peacock  looking backwards to the bogeys of the cold war rather than looking forward to the realities of the future in the various suggestions that he has made about Russian aid to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750819_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-24-0)

* The fact is that he still has a colonialist's view of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> and believes that even when independent it should still remain effectively an appendage of [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750819_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-24-0)

* <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750819_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-64-12)

* I direct a question to the Minister for Foreign Affairs which refers to the stated intention of the dissident group on Bougainville to declare independence from <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> on 1 September. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750821_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-14-0)

* -I would invite the honourable senator's attention to the statement issued by the Prime Minister on 1 1 August 1975 following discussions with the Chief Minister of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>,  Mr Michael  Somare. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750821_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-14-0)

* I will not read the whole of that statement, but the Prime Minister made the following points: It remains Australia's firm policy that <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> come to independence as one country in accordance with the wishes of the overwhelming majority of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>'s elected representatives. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750821_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-14-0)

* The Australian Government will give no sympathy, aid or support in any form to any group in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> working to undermine their country's unity. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750821_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-14-0)

* A unilateral declaration of independence, if given effect, would be an illegal act which could not itself alter in terms of the law of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>, the authority of the Government of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> over the whole of the territory of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>, or detract from Australia's international rights and duties under the trusteeship agreement. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750821_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-14-0)

* Any move for Bougainville to become independent before 16 September would require not only the assent of the Government of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> but also that of the Australian Government and the United Nations. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750821_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-14-0)

* The Prime Minister had given  Mr Somare  renewed assurances of Australian support and had every confidence that the move to independence on 16 September of a united <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> would proceed smoothly. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750821_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-14-0)

* 
 Mr Somare has sent a message to the Secretary-General of the United Nations stating that the Government of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> has no intention of agreeing to the separation of any part of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750821_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-14-0)

* I noted that there were plans for further discussions between the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Government and Bougainvillean representatives and I expressed the hope that these might provide opportunity for movement towards an accommodation between the central government and the Bougainvilleans. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750821_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-14-0)

* We have no national obligations or interest in getting rein.volved in colonial or post colonial affairs in Portuguese Timor at the very time when <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>'s imminent independence is leading to the ending of our colonial role there. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750826_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-42-0)

* I refer to clause  16  which expressly applies the Act on an extra-territorial basis so that it operates both within and outside Australia and extends to every external territory other than <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750826_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-57-0)

* The legislation which I now introduce is historic -for <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>, for Australia, and for the European civilisation from which we Australians spring. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750902_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-42-0)

* Australia was never truly free until <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> became truly free. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750902_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-42-0)

* The purpose of this legislation is to enable <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> to become independent on 16 September 1975, the date nominated by the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> House of Assembly. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750902_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-42-0)

* The legislation includes four Bills which are associated in various ways with <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>'s move to independence. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750902_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-42-0)

* This Bill gives effect to an announcement the then Minister Assisting the Minister for Foreign Affairs in matters relating to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> made on 1 6 September 1 974 that Australia would hand over to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> the administration of the Pocklington Reef Islands. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750902_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-48-0)

* These islands are a small uninhabited group 130 kilometres east of the southeastern tip of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750902_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-48-0)

* The Bill provides for the islands to be brought within the territorial scope of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>, so that at independence that country will exercise full sovereignty over the islands. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750902_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-48-0)

* The Bill also gives <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> authority to enact off-shore legislation in the area around the islands. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750902_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-48-0)

* <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> already has authority to enact legislation dealing with its off-shore adjacent areas as denned in the Australian Petroleum (Submerged Lands) Act, but these adjacent areas do not include Pocklington Reef Islands. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750902_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-48-0)

* Clause 4 of the Bill amends the present authorisation and enables <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> to enact legislation dealing with off-shore areas other than those to which the Australian Petroleum (Submerged Lands) Act applies. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750902_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-48-0)

* It also had responsibility for war graves generally in Australia and in external territories- <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>, the Solomon Islands- and for the Ambon war cemetery in Indonesia. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750904_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-13-0)

* I advised him that it was the Government's desire, because of the legislative timetable, to pass the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Bill 1975, the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Independence Bill 1975, the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Loans Guarantee Bill 1975, the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> (Staffing Assistance) Bill 1975, and the Social Services Bill (No. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750904_senate_29_s65/#debate-30)

* I reiterated to  Senator Withers  and pointed out to  Senator Guilfoyle  that it was the Government's desire to have these 5 <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Bills passed before the Senate rose today. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750904_senate_29_s65/#debate-30)

* The presentation of these Bills to the Senate marks the formal end of Australia's responsibilities for the Territories of Papua and New Guinea and the commencement of the formal responsibility of the Government of the newly independent country of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750904_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-35-0)

* I use the word 'formal' advisedly because over the past 12 years there has been an emerging responsibility by the local inhabitants of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> for the control of their own affairs. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750904_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-35-0)

* I think it is significant that these Bills should be appropriately marked by the recognition which is to be given to those many people who have contributed to the emergence of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> as a nation in circumstances which have not been marked by violent pressures on the part of the newly emerging country or in any way by resistance to the claims of nationhood by the country which had the responsibility in law for its government. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750904_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-35-0)

* The <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Independence Bill is, of course, the major Bill because it formally constitutes the act by Australia under which we acknowledge we no longer possess sovereignty and it is the measure by which the new nation finds itself on its own with a constitution of its own creation. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750904_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-35-0)

* The <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Independence Bill is a Bill which marks the end of Australia's responsibility. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750904_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-35-0)

* The <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Bill is a Bill which ensures that the uninhabited islands to the east of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> are formally within the sovereignty and control of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>, at least insofar as an Act of the Australian Parliament can make them. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750904_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-35-0)

* The <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> (Staffing Assistance) Bill is a Bill which conveniently transfers to Australia the responsibility which has been existing for the past 2 years and under which Australian citizens in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> have been working within the control and under the direction of the local Government. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750904_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-35-0)

* The <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Loans Guarantee Bill is a Bill which simply transfers Australia's guarantee for the moneys raised by the earlier Government of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> to the new nation of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750904_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-35-0)

* I consider it appropriate to refer to the preamble to the Bill, which is described as a Bill for an Act relating to the attainment of independence by <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750904_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-35-0)

* I stop there to indicate that part of the eastern half of that island which we know as <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> was always part of Australia. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750904_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-35-0)

* I think it is consistent with the wishes of both the Territory of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> and the Government of Australia that the action which is being taken by these Bills should be taken. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750904_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-35-0)

* One cannot foretell the future of the people of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750904_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-35-0)

* A second resolution was passed in 1969 by the House of Assembly which asserted that the time of selfgovernment and independence was for the people of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> to decide. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750904_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-35-0)

* I think the third resolution, in 1970, was that questions relating to changes in the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Act or changes in the constitutional structure of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> were for the members of the House of Assembly to determine. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750904_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-35-0)

* I would have thought, in what was generally a completely bipartisan approach by the parties which have alternated in government in Australia towards the question of independence for <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>, there was only one area in which there might have been any fluctuation or difference. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750904_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-35-0)

* I refer to the events which occurred in 1 970 as to whether or not the target which was being set for the people of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> was the target date which they would have set if they had been left to make a decision without targets being put before them. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750904_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-35-0)

* AND WHEREAS by virtue of the  <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Act  1971, the Territories governed in the Administrative union became together known as <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>: [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750904_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-35-0)

* He was but one of a host of dedicated young people, some of whom spent short periods, others longer periods, in the Territory of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> doing a job which I hope would be regarded as one which reflected great credit on the governments of Australia. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750904_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-35-0)

* There were various seminars and conferences which were arranged in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> in the late 1960s at which the people of Australia, including the present Governor-General, interested themselves intensely in the form which the ultimate independence of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> would take. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750904_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-35-0)

* There was a growth and extension of the role of civil authority and the acceptance of law throughout the Territory of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750904_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-35-0)

* I think it ought to be acknowledged that until approximately 4 years ago there were no indigenous lawyers in the Territory of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750904_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-35-0)

* Australian lawyers and Australian judges extended the rule of law throughout parts of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> which in some cases had not seen a white face prior to the early 1 950s. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750904_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-35-0)

* These events are part of the process by which the development of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> took place. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750904_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-35-0)

* From that stage onwards, both by statute in Australia and by steps which were gradually assumed by the people in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>, government was devolving increasingly upon the local people. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750904_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-35-0)

* AND WHEREAS on 9 July 1974 the House of Assembly resolved that <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> move to independent nation status: [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750904_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-35-0)

* AND WHEREAS the General Assembly of the United Nations on 13 December 1974 noted that resolution and resolved that, on the date on which <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> became independent, the Trusteeship Agreement would cease to be in force: [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750904_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-35-0)

* AND WHEREAS on 18 June 1975 the House of Assembly nominated 16 September 1975 as the date on which <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> is to become independent: [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750904_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-35-0)

* AND WHEREAS on 16 September 1975 <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> is to become an independent sovereign state by the name of the Independent State of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>, having a constitution established, adopted and given to themselves by the people of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> acting through their Constituent Assembly: [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750904_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-35-0)

* That is the procedure under which <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> will acquire its independence. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750904_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-35-0)

* But in the course of the discharging of that obligation I think Australia has been well served, as I believe the people of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> have been well served, by the persons who have contributed to the result which is about to emerge on 16 September. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750904_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-35-0)

* When one considers the Administrators of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> going back before the present Administrator-  Sir Hubert  Murray,  Sir Donald  Cleland,  Mr David  Hay and  Mr Les  Johnson- one acknowledges that the persons who assumed that position were persons who gave tremendous dedication to that Territory. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750904_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-35-0)

* There was a whole host of dedicated Australians, some of whom I have mentioned, and a whole host of dedicated people in the departments, in particular in the Department of the Interior and the Department of External Territories, who gave an enormous amount of their energy and skills to the emerging of selfgovernment in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750904_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-35-0)

* Of course, there was a host of Australians, some of whom still remain there today, who played their part in the passing scene of an earlier <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750904_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-35-0)

* There is no doubt that because of the size of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> and its geographical situation in relation to Australia, it is of great importance to us. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750904_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-35-0)

* There is no doubt that the new nation of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> will have great problems. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750904_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-35-0)

* I believe that even after 16 September when independence is granted to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>, Australia will still have a part to play- maybe in an advisory role- to assist <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> to be able to continue and prosper as a new nation. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750904_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-35-0)

* I believe also that Australia has a role to play on the financial side in assisting the new nation of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> to attain its aspirations. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750904_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-35-0)

* I believe that anything that we may do in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> will be a very good investment for the future. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750904_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-35-0)

* It would be a tragedy if a nation with doubtful intentions towards peaceful coexistence in South-East Asia- I refer particularly to some of the communist regimes to the northwere to make <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> financially dependent on it. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750904_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-35-0)

* Australia was never truly free until <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> became truly free. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750904_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-35-0)

* I am one who would hate to see the situation in which <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> became financially or otherwise dependent on some other nation that may threaten that particular independence. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750904_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-35-0)

* That is why I believe that whatever government is in power in Canberra, it has a responsibility to ensure that the new nation of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> does not become dependent on some other power. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750904_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-35-0)

* It is our responsibility, in the main, to ensure that <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> is assisted in every possible way. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750904_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-35-0)

* Of course, north Queensland, which is the area from which I come, has a particular interest in this regard because parts of the Queensland territory extend within a few hundred yards of the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> mainland. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750904_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-35-0)

* This is what he said in relation to the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Bill 1975: [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750904_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-35-0)

* The legislation which I now introduce is historic- for <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>, for Australia, and for the European civilisation from which we Australians spring. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750904_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-35-0)

* Australia was never truly free until <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> became truly free. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750904_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-35-0)

* In referring to the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Loans Guarantee Bill 1975 he said: [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750904_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-35-0)

* This Bill seeks the approval of Parliament to the continuation of the Australian Government guarantee, provided for in section 75a of the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Act 1949-1975, in respect of loans raised by the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Government from Australia and P.N.G. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750904_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-35-0)

* I would mention that loans <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> has raised from overseas sources are guaranteed until final maturity under separate legislation. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750904_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-35-0)

* The guarantees to be continued by this legislation and those provided in respect of overseas borrowings have assisted <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> in undertaking its borrowing programs. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750904_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-35-0)

* Then in referring to the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> (Staffing Assistance) Bill 1975 he said: [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750904_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-35-0)

* The purpose of this Bill is ... to introduce the new staffing aid arrangements which have recently been agreed between the Australian Government and the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Government. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750904_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-35-0)

* No doubt the Territory will become known after 16 September, which is less than 2 weeks away, as <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750904_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-35-0)

* One of the main worries with which this country will have to contend is not the communist countries to the north but the tentacles of the financial octopus of Japan and other countries, none of which is associated with communism, which have spread throughout <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750904_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-35-0)

* 1 think that would need to be the subject of consultation between the Government of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> and the Government of Australia. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750904_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-35-0)

* If there is a change of government in this country in the next 20 years, I hope that the role of friendship will continue to be played insofar as the people of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> are concerned. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750904_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-35-0)

* I am very proud to be associated with the passage of these Bills, having been one of those persons who have visited the Territory frequently over a period of 30 years, and who has many good friends not only within the Pangu Party but also in other political organisations in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750904_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-35-0)

* I am absolutely delighted to see that at long last that country is coming to nationhood, but I again emphasise the warning I have given that the people of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> need our friendship and our assistance. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750904_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-35-0)

* Regardless of what may be our station in life in Australia, there is a very big responsibility resting upon the people of this nation to ensure that <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> goes forward in a spirit of progress and of friendship with this country. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750904_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-35-0)

* The people of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> have been subjected to a rip-off by some unscrupulous business firms and by some unscrupulous countries including this country in days gone by, for almost 100 years. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750904_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-35-0)

* <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> is a grown-up nation. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750904_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-35-0)

* If we continue our spirit of friendship and mutual co-operation and assistance, <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> will go on to be a very proud country in the almost immediate future. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750904_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-35-0)

* A great number of florid speeches have been made about this tremendously important occasion on which the people of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> are to have power transferred to them that will enable them to become independent. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750904_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-35-0)

* There has been a forced draught process of trying to bring <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> to a state of independence as a result of pressures from the United Nations. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750904_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-35-0)

* Under this forced draught system of pressure from the United Nations the people of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> have the best independence that money can buy for them. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750904_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-35-0)

* There is very little left in terms of what might be called a social infrastructure in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> as distinct from a material infrastructure in the form of ports, harbours, jetties, bridges and roads. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750904_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-35-0)

* I made the forecast that 1974 would be the last year in which Australia could beneficially affect the people of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> and that from 1974 onwards the problem presented by <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> to Australia would be of an infinitely greater dimension than the problem it had presented in the past 10 years. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750904_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-35-0)

* I make this forecast, regretfully and with no pleasure: In the next 10 years <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> will present greater problems to Australia than it has presented under the forced draught system by which we have brought it to independence. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750904_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-35-0)

* The basic problem is that <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> is not an entity. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750904_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-35-0)

* In other words, the new nation of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> which we are ushering into independence in the next fortnight is what I describe as a centrifugal nation. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750904_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-35-0)

* The people of Bougainville, for example, are not Papua New Guineans in the sense that we understand the term. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750904_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-35-0)

* I do not think that the new nation of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> and its present Ministry realise the seriousness of the situation that is now developing in Bougainville. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750904_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-35-0)

* Members of my Party in the other place complained that Australia was behaving in a mean way towards the people of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> by making sure that the amount required under one of these Bills which relates to the golden handshake, as it is sometimes called, to be given to all the people who served that country for a long time honestly, with great courage and under enormous hardship will be part of the aid program. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750904_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-35-0)

* One was that the departure of Australians from <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> should carry with it the responsibility of the new nation at least to maintain the pensions of the people who had served that country. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750904_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-35-0)

* The only other option open- there are many illustrations of this- was for Australia itself to ensure that the expatriates who had worked in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> all their lives, some of them having been third generation people, had their pension rights protected. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750904_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-35-0)

* What happened, in essence, was that Australia said that <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> otherwise would have to pay so many millions of dollars a year towards the pensions of these expatriates; so Australia would pay the pensions and would carry out this obligation which in ethical, commercial and industrial terms <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> should accept. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750904_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-35-0)

* So it is of no good the Chief Minister of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>- I assume he will be the Prime Minister on 17 September- complaining that he has been unfairly treated. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750904_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-35-0)

* I think the Government has been perfectly correct in making the Ministry of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> realise that it has an obligation to accept some of the responsibilities of independence; that is, they will have to learn to stand on their own feet and not become a mendicant society. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750904_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-35-0)

* I refer honourable senators to the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Loans Guarantee Bill. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750904_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-35-0)

* That Bill relates to the guarantee of loans that have been raised by the future nation of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750904_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-35-0)

* The Bill will provide for a statutory guarantee by Australia in respect of repayment, on and after the date on which <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> attains independence. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750904_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-35-0)

* I wish the people of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> good fortune. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750904_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-35-0)

* Senator Greenwood  gave me very generous mention in his remarks on the various Bills relating to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> that are before the Senate. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750904_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-35-0)

* It is because of my very brief contact with the Territory, a period of some 2 years in the mid-1960s, that I wish to make at least some expression of goodwill to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> as it moves into independence. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750904_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-35-0)

* I rise merely because of my previous very close association with the people of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750904_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-35-0)

* It would be foolish for us today, when considering this rather momentous legislation, to ignore the problems that face the people and Government of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750904_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-35-0)

* In the early days of the 1 920s and 1930s they endured great hardship and showed tremendous courage in bringing some semblance of law and order in opening up the Territory of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750904_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-35-0)

* However, there is little we can do now as the responsibility rests with the Government of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750904_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-35-0)

* One hopes and trusts that self-government and independence in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> will be successful. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750904_senate_29_s65/#subdebate-35-0)

* 1 )  Has the Minister seen reports of a meeting in Brisbane last week between the Queensland Premier,  Mr BjelkePetersen,  and the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Minister for Information and Broadcasting, Dr Taureka [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19760518_senate_30_s68/#subdebate-53-70)

* The Commonwealth Government has been informed by Queensland Government officials that, contrary to media reports, the question of an offer of aid to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> by Queensland was not discussed with  Dr Taureka  during his visit to Brisbane. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19760518_senate_30_s68/#subdebate-53-70)

* As indicated in the reply to point  2  of the question, the Queensland Government did not make any offer of aid to  Dr Taureka  and the question of acceptance by the Government of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> does not therefore arise. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19760518_senate_30_s68/#subdebate-53-70)

* The purpose of this Bill is to amend the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> (Staffing Assistance) Act 1 973- 1 97 5 to wind up the Australian Staffing Assistance Group arrangements in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> on 30 June 1976. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19760601_senate_30_s68/#subdebate-48-0)

* The Australian Staffing Assistance Group was established under the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> (Staffing Assistance) Act 1973 and came into being on 1 December 1973, the date on which responsibility for the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Public Service was transferred to the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Government. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19760601_senate_30_s68/#subdebate-48-0)

* At that time there were some 4500 overseas officers of the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Public Service and the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Police Force who had been appointed as permanent officers or engaged as contract officers by former Ministers for External Territories under the former <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Act. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19760601_senate_30_s68/#subdebate-48-0)

* Under the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> (Staffing Assistance) Act 1973 these officers, together with a small number of temporary employees of the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Public Service and staff of the Electricity Commission who where contributors to the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Superannuation Fund, were separated from their respective <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> services and became the Australian Staffing Assistance Group, or ASAG, as it has become known. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19760601_senate_30_s68/#subdebate-48-0)

* The purpose of the Group was to make personnel available to occupy and carry out the duties of established positions in the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Public Service and other areas of public employment until Papua New Guineans became available to fill these positions, and the services of the ASAG personnel were no longer required. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19760601_senate_30_s68/#subdebate-48-0)

* The only personnel who have been added to the Australian Staffing Assistance Group since its establishment in 1973 have been those officers of the Australian and State Governments who have been seconded to ASAG for service in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19760601_senate_30_s68/#subdebate-48-0)

* In June last year the former Australian Prime Minister and the then Chief Minister- now Prime Minister- of Papua and New Guinea announced jointly that, following a review of staffing assistance arrangements, it has been agreed between the two Governments that the direct employment by Australia of the 2900 or so personnel who were then in ASAG- many occupying senior and influential positions in the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Public Service- was not in the immediate or long term interests of either [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19760601_senate_30_s68/#subdebate-48-0)

* In the meantime, new arrangements would be introduced to encourage those personnel in the Group whose services were still required, to transfer to direct contract employment with the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Government. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19760601_senate_30_s68/#subdebate-48-0)

* On Australia's part, the arrangements took the form of special conditions under which personnel could voluntarily terminate their employment in the Australian Staffing Assistance Group in order to accept contract employment with the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Government. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19760601_senate_30_s68/#subdebate-48-0)

* These conditions were settled after full consultation with the staff association representing ASAG employees, and included leave pay concessions, deferment or preservation of certain existing entitlements, accelerated payment of compensation instalments according to the period of contract service with <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>, and certain superannuation and retirement benefits concessions. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19760601_senate_30_s68/#subdebate-48-0)

* The <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> (Staffing Assistance) Act 1973 was amended in September 1975 to facilitate the introduction of these special conditions, the detailed provision of which will be made by regulations under the Act. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19760601_senate_30_s68/#subdebate-48-0)

* On <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>'s part, the new arrangements involved negotiation with the staff association of terms and conditions of contract employment broadly equivalent to those which applied to personnel of the Australian Staffing Assistance Group. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19760601_senate_30_s68/#subdebate-48-0)

* The <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> (Staffing Assistance) Termination Bill 1976, which is now before the Senate, consists of 34 clauses, most of which are of a machinery or 'savings' nature to preserve the residual entitlements of personnel when the Australian Staffing Assistance Group is wound up on 30 June 1 976. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19760601_senate_30_s68/#subdebate-48-0)

* To this end, the Bill provides that personnel of the Group who have not voluntarily terminated their employment by 30 June 1976, either to accept contract employment with the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Government or to return to Australia, will have their employment terminated on that date. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19760601_senate_30_s68/#subdebate-48-0)

* This is resulting in serious liquidity problems for both the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Superannuation Fund and the Contract Officers' Benefits Fund. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19760601_senate_30_s68/#subdebate-48-0)

* The Bill provides for the operation and administration of the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> schemes and two pre-war schemes- the Papua Superannuation Fund account and the New Guinea Superannuation Fund- to become, from 1 July 1976, the responsibility of the Commissioner for Superannuation, a position that will come into being under the Superannuation Act 1976 on that date. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19760601_senate_30_s68/#subdebate-48-0)

* Regulations are being prepared to enable those contributors to the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Superannuation Scheme, who so elect, to continue to contribute until the expiration of their first contract with the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Government or until 30 June 1978, whichever occurs first. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19760601_senate_30_s68/#subdebate-48-0)

* This, however, is a consequence of the speed with which events have moved in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>'s attainment of independence. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19760601_senate_30_s68/#subdebate-48-0)

* The Australian Staffing Assistance Group was devised as a mechanism to provide the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Government with the professional, technical and high level administrative expertise which it needed, particularly in the period between selfgovernment and independence. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19760601_senate_30_s68/#subdebate-48-0)

* The new arrangements under which personnel of the Australian Staffing Assistance Group are encouraged to transfer to direct contract employment with the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Government will, however, enable <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> to retain most of that expertise. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19760601_senate_30_s68/#subdebate-48-0)

* The Government has, however, made public statements of its intentions regarding future aid to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> and Indonesia, and of our prospective contributions to a number of international funds. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19760601_senate_30_s68/#subdebate-63-13)

* The forthcoming negotiations with <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> will aim at establishing a permanent and stable arrangement which will be accepted internationally and by all parties concerned. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19760603_senate_30_s68/#subdebate-66-1)

* The Chief Collector of Taxes for <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>: information is exchanged between the Commissioner of Taxation and the Chief Collector on a reciprocal basis in connection with the application of the laws of the two countries. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19760604_senate_30_s68/#subdebate-69-15)

* Among those present was the Minister of Justice for <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19760604_senate_30_s68/#subdebate-69-23)

* My question is: Is the Minister of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> a permanent member of the Standing Committee of Attorneys-General? [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19760604_senate_30_s68/#subdebate-69-23)

* Will the Minister explain to the Senate, in any case, what the Minister of Justice of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> was doing at the meeting of the Standing Committee of Attorneys-General? * The Agreement will come into force when notes are exchanged between the Government of Australia and the Government of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> notifying compliance with their respective legal requirements. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19761110_senate_30_s70/#subdebate-35-0)

* Trade between <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> and Australia has always been an important feature of the special relationship which exists between the 2 countries. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19761110_senate_30_s70/#subdebate-35-0)

* Since 1926 Australia has accorded special duty free entry to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> products. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19761110_senate_30_s70/#subdebate-35-0)

* In 1950 Australia obtained waivers from the General Agreement on Tariffs and Trade to accord extensive duty free treatment to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> primary and processed primary products. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19761110_senate_30_s70/#subdebate-35-0)

* At the present time 95 per cent of Australian imports from <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> enter free of duty. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19761110_senate_30_s70/#subdebate-35-0)

* <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> is an important market for Australian exports. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19761110_senate_30_s70/#subdebate-35-0)

* In 1975-76 Australian producers exported approximately $170m worth of goods to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19761110_senate_30_s70/#subdebate-35-0)

* This represented 49 per cent of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>'s total imports. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19761110_senate_30_s70/#subdebate-35-0)

* <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> is Australia's eleventh largest market for all exports and the third largest market for manufactured goods. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19761110_senate_30_s70/#subdebate-35-0)

* Until the Agreement just signed comes into force trade relations between Australia and <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> will continue to be governed by the Memorandum of Understanding relating to interim trade and commercial arrangements. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19761110_senate_30_s70/#subdebate-35-0)

* The Memorandum, which was signed in December 1973, was intended to cover trade relations between Australia and <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> in the period between self-government and independence. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19761110_senate_30_s70/#subdebate-35-0)

* Most of the trade between <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> and Australia has traditionally been free of duties and other restrictions. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19761110_senate_30_s70/#subdebate-35-0)

* The Agreement was drawn up on the basis of the following 3 aims: To continue and extend the duty free and concessional conditions of access for <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> exports into Australia; to allow the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Government to develop new industries and to protect them from import competition; and to enable the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Government to pursue its social and economic objectives through the encouragement of capital inflow consistent with its investment guidelines. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19761110_senate_30_s70/#subdebate-35-0)

* It was recognised by both countries that Australia, in entering into this Agreement, should retain the right to protect its industries where it is considered that they are threatened with serious injury by imports from <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19761110_senate_30_s70/#subdebate-35-0)

* Accordingly the Agreement provides that a free trade area is established consisting of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> and Australia and that subject to certain exceptions specified in the Agreement trade between the member states should be free of duties and other restrictive regulations of commerce. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19761110_senate_30_s70/#subdebate-35-0)

* For the information of honourable senators I present the following documents relating to defence arrangements between Australia and <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>: [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1977/19770223_senate_30_s71/#subdebate-34-0)

* A joint statement by the Australian Prime Minister and the Prime Minister of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>; [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1977/19770223_senate_30_s71/#subdebate-34-0)

* Two separate exchanges of letters between the Australian Minister for Defence and the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Minister for Defence, Foreign Relations and Trade, concerning consultations regarding the use of Australian loan personnel in politically sensitive situations and an arrangement for the supply support of the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Department of Defence by the Department of Defence, Australia. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1977/19770223_senate_30_s71/#subdebate-34-0)

* Honourable senators will recall that the Right Honourable the Prime Minister of Australia and the Right Honourable Michael Somare issued a joint statement in Port Moresby on 1 1 February which made mention of defence arrangements formally negotiated and agreed between  Sir Maori  Kiki and the Minister for Defence of the governments of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> and Australia respectively. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1977/19770223_senate_30_s71/#subdebate-34-0)

* The agreements then reached fulfil the Government's intention, as set out in the White Paper on Australian Defence that I presented to the Senate in November last year, to formalise defence arrangements with <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> in the near future. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1977/19770223_senate_30_s71/#subdebate-34-0)

* Honourable senators will note that they closely follow the arrangements in force during the interim period since <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> independence, as set out in documents tabled by my predecessor in the previous Government on 9 October 1975. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1977/19770223_senate_30_s71/#subdebate-34-0)

* They demonstrate, in a practical way, the importance Australia and <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> attach to a continuing and close relationship in the defence field. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1977/19770223_senate_30_s71/#subdebate-34-0)

* The agreement between the Australian and <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> governments to sustain their close co-operation in defence matters and the joint affirmation of their intention to consult at the request of either about matters affecting their common security is not the less historic because so readily agreed, nor the less significant- for each and for others- because their friendship is already so firmly and so openly established. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1977/19770223_senate_30_s71/#subdebate-34-0)

* This Senate may look with pleasure and with no little pride upon the fact that in this new era of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>'s independence and national sovereignty, it has joined with Australia to re-affirm a clear and mutual interest in close co-operation and consultation in defence matters. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1977/19770223_senate_30_s71/#subdebate-34-0)

* The <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Government continues to seek by direct negotiation between the 2 countries continuing support and co-operation in defence matters with Australia, not by any formal defence treaty but by mutually acceptable arrangements between the 2 governments and by frequent consultations. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1977/19770223_senate_30_s71/#subdebate-34-0)

* Honourable senators will note that under the arrangements, Australia will continue to assist in the development of the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> defence force through the defence co-operation program. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1977/19770223_senate_30_s71/#subdebate-34-0)

* This program, to which the Government has allocated some $12m this financial year, will be planned in close consultation with the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Government and will be responsive to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> priorities. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1977/19770223_senate_30_s71/#subdebate-34-0)

* I commend the Australia-<span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> defence arrangements to the Senate. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1977/19770223_senate_30_s71/#subdebate-34-0)

* by leave- I present a statement relating to Australia and <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>, negotiations on maritime boundaries, and on other matters relating to the Torres Strait. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1978/19780511_senate_31_s77/#subdebate-44-0)
