[[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1978/19780511_senate_31_s77/#subdebate-44-0)

* Honourable members will know that Australia and <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> have been engaged in these negotiations over a period of years, beginning before <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> moved to independence in 1975. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1978/19780511_senate_31_s77/#subdebate-44-0)

* There could be no such lines until <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> became independent. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1978/19780511_senate_31_s77/#subdebate-44-0)

* The Australian and <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> governments have approached the negotiations with great care and concern in order to arrive at a solution which is equitable in human terms and lasting and beneficial in its consequences. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1978/19780511_senate_31_s77/#subdebate-44-0)

* In a statement on 3 1 March 1978 I said that research had shown that the small uninhabited islands of Kawa, Mata Kawa and Kussa, which lie very close to the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> mainland but which have often been shown on maps as part of Queensland, were not among the Torres Strait islands annexed to Queensland in the last century. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1978/19780511_senate_31_s77/#subdebate-44-0)

* I added that the Australian Government had accordingly informed the Government of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> that, in the eventual treaty, Australia would recognise them as part of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1978/19780511_senate_31_s77/#subdebate-44-0)

* After the Second World War that Territory was administered in union with the Territory of New Guinea and, as the Third Schedule to the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Act 1 949, as amended up to the time of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>'s independence, makes clear, islands within the Torres Strait that were not part of the State of Queensland continued to be within the bounds of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> immediately prior to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>'s independence. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1978/19780511_senate_31_s77/#subdebate-44-0)

* It will be clear from what I have said about the status of the Kawa and Kussa Islands that no question arises about any transfer of Australian territory to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1978/19780511_senate_31_s77/#subdebate-44-0)

* <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> sovereignty over those islands will be recognised in the treaty. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1978/19780511_senate_31_s77/#subdebate-44-0)

* There will be a delimitation of the territorial seas between Boigu, Dauan and Saibai and <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1978/19780511_senate_31_s77/#subdebate-44-0)

* In my statement to Parliament on 11 May 1978 I informed honourable members that in recent negotiations with the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Minister for Foreign Affairs and Trade,  Mr Ebia  Olewale, we agreed upon the principal basic elements which are to be included in the treaty to be concluded on maritime boundaries between our two countries and on other matters relating to Torres Strait. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1978/19780525_senate_31_s77/#subdebate-37-0)

* In this statement I wish to present to honourable senators an account of the principal basic elements which the Australian and <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Foreign Ministers have agreed will be included in the treaty. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1978/19780525_senate_31_s77/#subdebate-37-0)

* The Foreign Minister of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> is presenting a similar account to his Parliament. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1978/19780525_senate_31_s77/#subdebate-37-0)

* Before proceeding to speak about the treaty elements, I wish to recall that Australia and <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> have been engaged in these negotiations over a period of years, beginning before <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> moved to independence. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1978/19780525_senate_31_s77/#subdebate-37-0)

* Secondly, the package of elements which is now emerging provides for a fair and equitable division of sea and seabed resources between <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> and Australia across the whole area traversed by the proposed lines of delimitation. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1978/19780525_senate_31_s77/#subdebate-37-0)

* Fourthly, arrangements will be established in the Torres Strait area which are designed to meet fully the particular needs of the people of the area, including the people of the adjacent coastal area of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>, with regard to traditional movements and traditional fishing. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1978/19780525_senate_31_s77/#subdebate-37-0)

* In the treaty, Australia will recognise <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> sovereignty over the islands of Kawa, Mata Kawa and Kussa; <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> will recognise Australian sovereignty over all the Australian islands in the Torres Strait shown on map II as lying north of the seabed line. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1978/19780525_senate_31_s77/#subdebate-37-0)

* As shown on the maps, the territorial seas of the Australian islands north of the seabed line, and of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> in the area between Boigu and Dauan, will be a maximum of three nautical miles, and a territorial sea boundary will be delimited between Boigu, Dauan and Saibai and <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1978/19780525_senate_31_s77/#subdebate-37-0)

* The licensing arrangements will have regard to the desirability of promoting economic development and employment opportunities in the Torres Strait area including the adjacent coastal area of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>, and the people of the area will be consulted about these arrangements. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1978/19780525_senate_31_s77/#subdebate-37-0)

* Subject to the phasing arrangements specified in the paper I have tabled, the sharing of the commercial Protected Zone fisheries will be on the basis that Australia will have an overall share of 25 per cent of the commercial fisheries in waters under <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> jurisdiction; <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> will have an overall share of 25 per cent of the commercial fisheries in waters under Australian jurisdiction. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1978/19780525_senate_31_s77/#subdebate-37-0)

* The share in the territorial seas of the Australian uninhabited islands north of the seabed line other than Turnagain, however, will be on a 50/50 basis and <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> will have 100 per cent of the commercial barramundi fishery near the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> coast, excluding the territorial seas of Saibai, Dauan and Boigu. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1978/19780525_senate_31_s77/#subdebate-37-0)

* Third state operators will not normally be licensed to exploit those fisheries unless agreed by Australia and <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1978/19780525_senate_31_s77/#subdebate-37-0)

* Outline of principal basic elements agreed upon on S May, 1978 between the Foreign Ministers of Australia and <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> to be included in the treaty to be concluded on maritime boundaries between their two countries and on other matters relating to Torres Strait. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1978/19780525_senate_31_s77/#subdebate-37-0)

* Australia will recognise <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> sovereignty over the islands of Kawa, Mata Kawa and Kussa and the smaller islands appurtenant to those islands and over their territorial seas, subject to delimitation as necessary to be specified in the treaty. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1978/19780525_senate_31_s77/#subdebate-37-0)

* <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> will recognise Australian sovereignty over the inhabitated islands of Boigu, Dauan and Saibai and the smaller islands appurtenant to these islands, including Aubusi, Moimi and Kaumag and over the nine Australian uninhabited islands lying north of  the seabed delimitation line, that is Turu Cay, Kerr Islet, Deliverance Island, Turnagain Island, Pearce Cay, Black Rocks, Bramble Cay, Anchor Cay and East Cay, and over the three-mile territorial seas  or  those islands, subject to an agreed description of the delimitation thereof which will appear in the treaty. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1978/19780525_senate_31_s77/#subdebate-37-0)

* The territorial seas of Australia and <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> between Boigu and <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>, and between Dauan and Saibai and <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>, will be delimited along two agreed lines as broadly indicated on the maps. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1978/19780525_senate_31_s77/#subdebate-37-0)

* The breadth of the territorial sea of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> along its southern coastline between the meridians 142 03' 30" East and 142 5 1' 00" East will bea maximum of three miles and will not extend south of the two territorial sea delimitation lines or the straight line linking them as indicated on the maps. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1978/19780525_senate_31_s77/#subdebate-37-0)

* The extent of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> territorial sea, which will not in any event extend into the area south of the agreed seabed line, agreed areas of Australian territorial sea to the north of the seabed line, or the agreed area of Australian fisheries jurisdiction north of the seabed line, will depend on the base lines or archipelagic lines adopted by <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> in accordance with international law. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1978/19780525_senate_31_s77/#subdebate-37-0)

* Australia and <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> will not in future extend their territorial seas across the seabed delimitation line. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1978/19780525_senate_31_s77/#subdebate-37-0)

* The treaty will provide for equitable arrangements to be made by <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> in respect of the holders of the Australian petroleum permit Q/10P in those parts of the permit area that will fall on the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> side of the seabed delimitation line. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1978/19780525_senate_31_s77/#subdebate-37-0)

* In the administrative process of issuing licences, the relevant authorities of the two countries will have regard to the desirability of promoting economic development in the Torres Strait area including the adjacent coastal area of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> and employment opportunities for the people of the area. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1978/19780525_senate_31_s77/#subdebate-37-0)

* Provided these levels remain within the optimum sustainable yield of the fishery concerned, they will not be reduced for five years from the date of entry into force of the treaty but, over the subsequent five years, levels of 'take' may be adjusted progressively so that <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> will have an overall share of 25 per cent of the 'take' of the commercial Protected Zone fisheries in waters under Australian jurisdiction and Australia will have an overall share of 25 per cent of the 'take' of the commercial Protected Zone fisheries in waters under <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> jurisdiction, subject to the following: [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1978/19780525_senate_31_s77/#subdebate-37-0)

* In the territorial seas of the Australian uninhabited islands north of the seabed line, other than Turnagain, the 'sharing-of-take' formula will be 50 per cent Australia/50 per cent <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1978/19780525_senate_31_s77/#subdebate-37-0)

* <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> will have 100 percent of the take' in the commercial barramundi fishery near the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> coast: excluding the territorial seas of Saibai, Dauan and Boigu, and this 'take' will not be included in calculating the overall percentage share of' take'in the commercial protected Zone fisheries under the agreed sharing-of-take ' formula mentioned above. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1978/19780525_senate_31_s77/#subdebate-37-0)

* I refer the Minister representing the Minister for Foreign Affairs to two statements made by  Mr Michael  Somare, the Prime Minister of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1978/19780817_senate_31_s78/#subdebate-22-0)

* In reply to a question from  Mr John  Noel, who asked whether or not <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> should seek to enter into a defence treaty relationship with Australia before it is too late,  Mr Somare  said that he would rather not have <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> enter into a treaty relationship with Australia, given the special understanding between the two nations. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1978/19780817_senate_31_s78/#subdebate-22-0)

* What would be the present Government's attitude if the Government of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> approached Australia with the request for a formal defence pact? [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1978/19780817_senate_31_s78/#subdebate-22-0)

* In saying that I would set aside <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> which, as a Melanesian nation, has its own special relationship with Australia. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1978/19780817_senate_31_s78/#subdebate-41-0)

* While Australia has responsibilities towards <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> this does not relegate other countries to a secondary position in our considerations. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1978/19780817_senate_31_s78/#subdebate-41-0)

* The theme is supportive even allowing for our special relationship with <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1978/19780817_senate_31_s78/#subdebate-41-0)

* As honourable senators may very well know, for two years it was my privilege to be what was called the Australasian representative on the executive of the Commonwealth Parliamentary Association, and within my area were not only the parliaments of the Commonwealth of Australia and New Zealand, but also the parliaments or legislatures of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>, the Solomon Islands, the Gilbert Islands, Tuvalu, Fiji, Niue, Tonga and the Cook Islands. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1978/19780817_senate_31_s78/#subdebate-41-0)

* The National Library of Australia has been very much involved in setting up that library, both in its construction and in its collection and, indeed, in the programs which will provide an information resource centre for <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1978/19780817_senate_31_s78/#subdebate-41-0)

* <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> is one of the largest states. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1978/19780817_senate_31_s78/#subdebate-41-0)

* I am not aware ofthe number of residents of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> who have been engaged in the activities mentioned by  Senator Maunsell  but I am aware that Papua New Guinean citizens employed temporarily on a seasonal basis on Australian pearling and other vessels in the Torres Strait have not applied in the past to Australian immigration authorities for permission to engage in such employment. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1978/19780913_senate_31_s78/#subdebate-9-0)

* From information made available to me by the Minister for Immigration and Ethnic Affairs, I understand that on average the pearling season in the Torres Strait extends over nine months and that at the conclusion of the season it is customary for pearling vessel operators to return those Papua New Guineans employed on their vessels to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1978/19780913_senate_31_s78/#subdebate-9-0)

* The task force formed in the Department of Immigration and Ethnic Affairs to inquire into the movement of Papua New Guineans in the Torres Strait area and in mainland Australia has examined the matter of Papua New Guineans employed temporarily on Australian pearling vessels in the Torres Strait, and policy considerations involved in regularising the situation from an immigration point of view are currently under review by that task force. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1978/19780913_senate_31_s78/#subdebate-9-0)

* In conjunction with this program, the Division of Animal Health has also been co-ordinating the regular bloodsampling in 5 1 cattle herds scattered around Australia and <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1978/19780914_senate_31_s78/#subdebate-34-0)

* The specified categories are children under the age of 1 8 years; crew members; diplomats; persons who arrive in Australia but are deemed under the Migration Act 1958 not to have entered Australia, that is persons who remain at the airport and persons who do not disembark from a ship; persons covered by the Status of Forces Agreements with the United States of America and <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>; and persons being deported or extradited from Australia. * I refer to the Australian aid program for the South Pacific region and <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1978/19781025_senate_31_s79/#subdebate-9-0)

* In 1976 this Government announced the present long term commitment of economic and social aid to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>, thereby both raising the level of aid and establishing it on a five-year basis. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1978/19781025_senate_31_s79/#subdebate-9-0)

* Subject to normal parliamentary procedures of appropriation, Australia guaranteed to provide a minimum of $180m in social and economic aid to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> for each of the five years beginning on 1 July 1976 with annual supplements in the light of circumstances. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1978/19781025_senate_31_s79/#subdebate-9-0)

* The agreement put to an end the previous arrangements under which Australia had been involved in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>'s budget making. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1978/19781025_senate_31_s79/#subdebate-9-0)

* This aid relationship reflects <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>'s independent status and has provided a firm basis for that country's long term forward planning. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1978/19781025_senate_31_s79/#subdebate-9-0)

* The Minister for Foreign Affairs has appointed  Sir John  Crawford to advise him on means by which the aid arrangements with <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> can be developed further. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1978/19781025_senate_31_s79/#subdebate-9-0)

* As to the South Pacific, during the first year of office of this Government the decision was taken to introduce innovations in the aid program for the South Pacific, other than <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>, to meet its particular requirements. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1978/19781025_senate_31_s79/#subdebate-9-0)

[[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1978/19781107_senate_31_s79/#subdebate-66-0)

* It was in these capacities that during the recess I visited Port Moresby in <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> on the occasion of the presentation and opening of the new <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> National Library. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1978/19781107_senate_31_s79/#subdebate-69-0)

* The <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> National Library was Australia's independence gift and was officially presented by the Australian Prime Minister,  Mr Malcolm  Fraser, and opened by the Prime Minister of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>,  Mr Somare. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1978/19781107_senate_31_s79/#subdebate-69-0)

* The establishment of a national library was approved by the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> Government in January 1975. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1978/19781107_senate_31_s79/#subdebate-69-0)

* A task force of Australian officials from the National Library and from the Department of Foreign Affairs has been in New Guinea and has been in touch with <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> officials, and, in particular, with  Sir John  Yocklunn, the National Librarian of the <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> National Library. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1978/19781107_senate_31_s79/#subdebate-69-0)

* I would add that it is the Library itself that will be of most value to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1978/19781107_senate_31_s79/#subdebate-69-0)

* The contribution from the Australian people will give the National Library of Australia a continuing connection with <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>, a continuing interest in its library services and, indeed, a continuing involvement in all the benefits that a library brings to any community. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1978/19781107_senate_31_s79/#subdebate-69-0)

* The film collection, which is of considerable value, has some 6,000 titles and will be of the greatest assistance in the development of library services to the community of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1978/19781107_senate_31_s79/#subdebate-69-0)

* The guidelines for this and for other related matters concerning the Library were laid down by the National Librarian of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span>,  Sir John  Yocklunn. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1978/19781107_senate_31_s79/#subdebate-69-0)

* We are indebted, I think, to the Royal Australian Air Force transport unit for its assistance in the transportation of materials from Australia to <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> prior to the opening of its National Library. * This took its place alongside the local collection of what is called, I believe, Papua New Guineana, which is now housed in a special and carefully preserved area. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1978/19781107_senate_31_s79/#subdebate-69-0)

* I am indeed very well pleased with it and I am sure it will be a great asset to the community of <span class="highlight">Papua New Guinea</span> and form a worthy independence gift. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1978/19781107_senate_31_s79/#subdebate-69-0)
